Sixth and Seventh General Meetings Yesterday

Chairman Mu's Report 142

The National Industry and Commerce Conference held its sixth general meeting at 9:00 AM on the 7th at the Lizhi Society. The presidium members Hu Shuhua, Zhou Dian, and Li Kuian attended. Chairman Mu Ouchu reported that the conference would be held for five hours yesterday afternoon and evening, but if the discussions could be conducted quickly, there could be a two-hour break in the afternoon. Currently, in addition to reviewing the reports, there are several provisional motions being printed.

Third Report of the Second Group 143

First, Li Kuian, the reviewing member of the second group, reported the third report of the second group as follows:

Full Text of the Review Report of the Second Group 144

Encourage Overseas Chinese to Ship Red and Green Tea Overseas

Discontinue Ordnance Factories and Remodel New-Style Agricultural Tools

Develop Export Industries in the Northeast

41. Concerning the proposal to request the establishment of overseas industry and commerce investigation offices (Tang Changfeng): This proposal provides very detailed planning for overseas industry and commerce investigation matters. It is proposed that the General Assembly approve it and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce adopt it.

42. Recommendation on maintaining egg trade with the United States (Tianjin Xinji Trading Company, etc.): The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has just recovered the inspection of foreign personnel handling inspections in China. If the proposed method is followed, it seems inappropriate. However, resolving foreign trade disputes is of great importance, and it is proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce promptly formulate other relief measures. 43. Proposal that state-owned railways promptly establish warehouse operations, vigorously implement responsible cargo transportation, and issue custody receipts and shipping receipts to regulate the economy of merchants and the people (Ding Jingchen, Zhong Weichen): The matters raised in this proposal are all things that should be done. It is proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce consult the Ministry of Railways to adopt and implement them.

44. Because of the decline of Chinese tea and the hardship of the people's livelihood, it is proposed to persuade overseas Chinese to try to ship red and green tea overseas, promote domestic goods, and relieve the people's livelihood (Yu Duwei): The proposal advocates maintaining the tea industry and is consistent with the opinion of the eighth case in the previous review report of this group. It is proposed that they be merged and handled.

45. The government should give special encouragement and protection to foreign trade (

Lu Chengchang): The methods listed in this proposal are all appropriate. It is proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce adopt them.

46. Please implement an incentive policy to develop the export trade of the Northeast (Lu Guangji): This proposal involves the reduction of freight rates and tariffs, which concerns the Ministries of Finance and Railways. It is proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce forward it to the Ministries of Finance and Railways for consideration.

47. Establish a temporary specialized committee to investigate the main export goods of the country in order to increase production, improve quality, and develop foreign trade (

He Lian, Fang Xianting): This proposal advocates setting up a committee to investigate the main export products in order to develop foreign trade, which is of great importance. It is proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce adopt and implement it. 48. Establish overseas commercial counselors to promote international trade (He

Lian, Fang Xianting): This proposal is consistent with the first item of the first proposal. It is proposed that it be referred for joint study.)

49. Proposal to convert the discontinued ordnance factories and mints into industrial factories and give priority to manufacturing new-style agricultural tools (He Cen): This proposal proposes to convert the discontinued ordnance factories, mints, and other factories into industrial factories, which is a very good intention. It is proposed that it be passed and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce consult the competent authorities in each province to conduct thorough investigations and promote the conversion.

Each Proposal Passed Through Discussion 145

After the report, the chairman asked if there were any objections to the above nine proposals. If there were no objections, they would be considered passed. The entire assembly had no objections and decided to pass them.

Third Review Report of the Third Group Passed 146

Next, the third review report of the third group was discussed, and Yan Zhuang reported as follows:

Case 34 (Qian Chengxu, etc.): The case is about the proposal to amend Article 18 of the Factory Law. After review, this case falls within the scope of legal interpretation and does not need to be submitted for amendment.

Case 35 (Wang Yunwu): The case is to request that all industries and factories be ordered to stipulate work standards in order to increase production and reduce labor-management disputes. After review, this case should be discussed together with Case 31 of this group.

Case 36 (Liu Kai): The case is about stipulating minimum wage measures. After review, the measures in this case should be revised as follows: "First, establish wage committees in industrially developed areas, organized by representatives from the government, labor, and management, to stipulate the minimum wage rates for each industry based on local living conditions and submit them to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce (or a separately organized central wage committee) for approval and implementation." And request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to handle the matter (passed).

Discussing Scientific Management

Principle Passed 147

In addition, there is the scientific management method proposal submitted by the Zhejiang Construction Department, which was reported by Wang Yunwu. This case was merged from the scientific management method cases and the industrial rationalization cases into this case. The third group designated Liu Hongsheng and himself to be responsible for reviewing it and submitted this case as follows:

Proposal to promote scientific management methods in order to achieve industrial rationalization

(Explanation) This case is based on the Proposal to Promote the Scientific Management of Industry submitted by the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department, the Proposal to Promote Scientific Management Methods submitted by the Industry and Commerce Visiting Bureau, the Request to Implement Scientific Management Methods in National Industry and Commerce submitted by Chen Ting'an, the Proposal to Request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to Order All Industries and Factories to Stipulate Work Standards to Increase Production and Reduce Labor-Management Disputes submitted by Wang Yunwu, the Proposal to Plan to Establish Industrial and Commercial Management Personnel Training Institutes submitted by Xu PeiHuang, and the Proposal to Establish a Central Industrial Rationalization Research Association and Establish Research Branches in Various Provinces and Cities submitted by the Zhejiang Construction Department. The Proposal to Promote Rationalization to Establish the Foundation of Industry and Commerce submitted by Mu Junde and the opinions of member Wang Yunwu were merged to form this case. (Reason) Scientific management methods are methods to promote production, eliminate consumption, and eliminate labor-management disputes. They originated in the United States and France and spread to countries around the world. Industrial rationalization (is a whole plan for the national economy, which originated in Germany and was decided by the International Economic Conference, hoping that countries around the world will adopt it together. The former is a means, the latter is a goal, the former has a narrower meaning and is suitable for an industry or an institution, the latter has a broader meaning and is suitable for an entire profession or the entire country. Although their sources and meanings are slightly different, they are no different in their suitability to the current needs of our country. Because our country's industry is fragile, and the number of people surpassing it each year is as high as tens of thousands of yuan. To resist foreign economic aggression, it is impossible to develop domestic industry without success. To develop industry and make the quality, quantity, and value of domestic products sufficient to compete with foreign goods, there is no other way than to strictly implement scientific management methods. Also, there are many labor-management disputes at present, which have caused the embryonic industry to be destroyed again. However, after studying the reasons, most of them are due to the inadequacy and unfairness of labor remuneration. Scientific management methods can obtain the maximum production with the minimum labor and the lowest

Consumption, the result is the possibility of making labor remuneration adequate. Scientific management methods stipulate work standards according to objective methods, and the result is the possibility of making labor remuneration fair. Therefore, scientific management methods are undoubtedly an essential plan for our country's industrial sector. As far as industrial rationalization is concerned, the current economic chaos in our country is no different from that of Germany after the war. Germany used industrial rationalization to make the national economy a whole plan to save the country's fortune. Therefore, our country also needs to learn from it. (Measures) (A) Regarding scientific management methods (1) The Ministry of Industry and Commerce should issue an order to the provincial and municipal governments to supervise industrial and commercial administrative

The organs convene industrial and commercial leaders to organize branches of the China Industrial and Commercial Management Association to study the implementation plan of scientific management methods (2) The Ministry of Industry and Commerce should order all industries and factories to stipulate work standards within a possible scope and give bonuses to workers who exceed the standards on a regular basis (3) The National Industry and Commerce Conference should issue a declaration unanimously supporting the research and implementation of scientific management methods (B) Regarding industrial rationalization (1) The central government should set up a National Industrial Rationalization Research Association (2) The National Industrial Rationalization Research Association should aim to study the entire plan of the national economy (3) The National Industrial Rationalization Research Association should be organized by the following organs and groups (A) The central organs in charge of and related to industrial administrative affairs, such as the Construction Committee, the Ministry of Finance, Industry and Commerce, Agriculture and Mining, Communications, and Railways (B) Academic groups such as the China Industrial and Commercial Management Association, the China Science Society, the China Engineering Society, the China Economic Society, and the Chinese Agricultural Society (C) National vocational groups such as the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, etc. Those who have not organized a national association shall temporarily be replaced by vocational groups in important cities such as the Shanghai Bankers Association (D) Representatives of labor groups (4) The organs and groups in the preceding article shall separately appoint several representatives as basic members (5) The basic members shall elect several experts who do not belong to the organs and groups in Article 3 to form the National Industrial Rationalization Research Association Committee with the basic members (6) Several subcommittees shall be established

The personnel of the organs and groups in Article 3 shall organize them, but they do not belong to this

Personnel of item organs and groups may also join (7) The National Industrial Rationalization Research Association shall set up a fixed administrative department and a research department (8) The National Industrial Rationalization Research Association shall be allocated funds by the central government (9) The National Industrial Rationalization Research Association shall be designated by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to appoint members and hire experts as preparatory members for preparation

Discussion Situation 148

After Wang Yunwu's report, Bi Fangjiaobo said that Wang's report was detailed and the methods were very appropriate. He requested the chairman to put it to a vote. The chairman said that the above four proposals could be combined and put to a vote. Zheng Hongnian said that under the "various academic organizations" item in the third proposal, "various universities" should be added and not just individuals. The chairman said that scientific management should not waste time, energy, or materials; only when the above three points can be implemented does it conform to the principles of scientific management.

Yang Xifo said that regarding the organizations researching industrial rationalization, besides the various universities, there is also the Construction Committee, etc. However, the equipment, talent, etc., of research associations across the country may not be able to bear this significant responsibility. He proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce organize an industrial rationalization research association, using national financial resources to gather national talent to conduct research. Wang Yunwu explained that the seventh proposal called for a fixed secretariat and research department to be established in the rationalization research association to be responsible for research, and that it did not include convening all national talent, as that would be difficult to achieve in practice.

Zhu Maocheng said that the situations of industrial rationalization research associations vary in different countries, and their purpose is to invent new methods of rationalization. China's industrial rationalization research association is indeed urgently needed at present.

Shi Ying advocated soliciting research from domestic organizations and individuals separately, so he proposed that the principle of this proposal be passed first, and then the implementation methods be reviewed and handled by the Ministry of Industry. A representative from Zhejiang Province said that the purpose of proposing this proposal should be to request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to establish a research association to collect specialized talent to engage in research and publish the research results to the industrial and commercial sectors for them to learn from. Therefore, the importance of this proposal is not something that empty academic research organizations can fulfill. A member proposed to stop the discussion and put it to a vote.

The chairman announced the end of the discussion. The principle of this proposal was passed, and the detailed methods were handed over to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for review and handling. The resolution was passed.

Most Urgent to Commander-in-Chief Chiang in Fenghua, and please forward to all armed comrades at the front: The recent Yan-Feng Rebellion has caused turmoil throughout the country. Fortunately, Your Excellency has upheld the late Premier's teachings with a spirit of fearlessness, leading armed comrades to serve the country, thereby quelling the rebellion, removing obstacles, and allowing our industrial and commercial circles to see the light of day again. Gathered in the capital under a unified and consolidated government, we can calmly discuss all construction issues. In terms of the Party and the Nation, this is regarded as a harbinger of better times after adversity. From the industrial and commercial standpoint, it is especially recognized as a new opportunity for survival and revival. The conference proposes to support the Central Government in quelling the rebellion, consolidating peace and unity, and protecting industry and commerce to develop the economy. Please circulate this telegram throughout the country to clarify the justice of right and wrong and to offer condolences to General Commander Chiang and the armed comrades at the front. The proposal lists three measures: (1) This conference will send telegrams to General Commander Chiang and the armed comrades at the front to offer condolences and circulate a telegram throughout the country to analyze the right and wrong, and to establish national policy. (2) This conference will raise funds to build a memorial tower in the capital to commemorate the quelling of this rebellion. (3) The chairman of this conference will lead the entire body in standing in silence for three minutes to express mourning for the soldiers who died in the front lines. The entire assembly unanimously passed the resolution to stabilize the situation and support the endangered, deeply moved by the virtue of your arrival. We pledge to exert our utmost efforts to support you with sincerity. This telegram is respectfully submitted for your consideration. Sincerely, all members of the National Industrial and Commercial Conference.

Second Report of the Fourth Group 150

The commercial tax section of the fourth group has been handed over with fifteen draft proposals for the second time, and seven draft proposals transferred from other groups. After review, opinions are as follows: Case No. 64: The Ministry of Railways should abolish railway freight donations and various miscellaneous donations. (Review Opinion) Railway freight donations and various miscellaneous donations are similar to transit taxes and should be abolished. The National Government has already issued a clear order to implement this on a fixed schedule, and it should be included in the abolition of transit tax cases.

Case No. 68: Wang Jiean of Yaoming Mast Light Factory requests tax exemption to receive equal treatment with Daming Company. (Review Opinion) Whether to exempt taxes on imitation foreign goods should be treated the same across the board. It should be resolved by the meeting and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities for review and handling.

Case No. 69: Hui Shu Kong's additional tax is too high. Please thoroughly cancel it to level the appraisal. (Review Opinion) This additional salt tax hinders sales and should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities for verification and handling.

Case No. 74: Tianjin Social Bureau requests a special import tax on cotton yarn to subsidize commercial cotton yarn factories. (Review Opinion) Whether the special tax on cotton yarn is uniform for both Chinese and foreign cotton yarn, or only levied on imported cotton yarn, is currently unknown. If it is uniform for both Chinese and foreign cotton yarn, then the subsidy method mentioned in the original proposal may be difficult to implement. It should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities for consideration.

Case No. 76: Tianjin Social Bureau pre-collects public welfare donations from merchants when purchasing local goods. (Review Opinion) The so-called public welfare donation seems to be establishing a separate item in addition to the regular tax. Once this precedent is set, various exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous taxes will inevitably be retained under various pretexts, and goods will still inevitably suffer heavy levies. This proposal should be rejected by the conference.

Case No. 80: Deng Yanhua requests that foreign machinery that cannot be manufactured domestically be exempted from taxes or reduced to the minimum to reduce the cost of manufactured goods. (Review Opinion) The domestic machinery industry is still in its infancy, and the tax rates should be reduced to develop industries. It should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities for appropriate reduction when revising import tariffs.

Case No. 81: Beijing General Chamber of Commerce requests the abolition of the Chongwenmen tax. (Review Opinion) The Chong Customs has already been resolved by the Executive Yuan to be abolished, so the conference does not need to discuss it.

Case No. 82: Tianjin General Chamber of Commerce requests the abolition of freight donations along the Ping-Sui Railway. (Review Opinion) The same as Case No. 64, it should be resolved by the conference and included in the abolition of transit tax cases.

Case No. 83: Tianjin General Chamber of Commerce requests a reduction or exemption of the excessive porcelain tax. (Review Opinion) The Hebei transit tax mentioned in the original proposal should be included in the abolition of transit tax cases. As for the excessively high Jiangxi special tax rate, it should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities for appropriate reduction.

Case No. 84: Tianjin General Chamber of Commerce requests that the Hebei Province unified tax is too high, please restore the old 1.25 system. (Review Opinion) After the implementation of the abolition of transit taxes, all Hebei Province unified taxes are being separately reorganized and abolished. At present, the province's unified tax is too high and repeatedly levied, and it should be resolved by the meeting and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities to quickly reduce or exempt it.

Case No. 86: Tianjin General Chamber of Commerce: The cessation of redemption of Zhili Provincial Bank banknotes is detrimental to merchants and residents. It is proposed to consult and transfer to the Hebei Provincial Government to maintain the original agreement to use reed salt production donations for reorganization. (Review Opinion) The reed salt production donation was originally designated specifically for the Zhili Provincial Bank's cash redemption, which concerns financial credit and cannot be ignored. It should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to earnestly consult the Hebei Provincial Government to handle it according to the old plan, and not to divert it for other purposes to alleviate merchants' difficulties.

Case No. 87: Beijing Shuanghesheng requests that all foreign wines in concessions be uniformly affixed with stamps. (Review Opinion) The original proposal states that the stamp tax burden on foreign wines in concessions and domestically produced imitation wines is uneven, which is indeed the case. It should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities to handle it to ensure that the burden is equal.

Case No. 88: Hangzhou National Goods Factory Joint Association requests exemption from national goods advertising donations. (Review Opinion) Advertising is indeed an exorbitant tax and miscellaneous tax that hinders the promotion of merchants' goods. Please resolve by the conference and consult with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for exemption. In addition, if other provinces have such exorbitant donations, they should be handled uniformly.

Case No. 89: Shanghai Cosmetics Trade Association requests an increase in import finished goods tax and exemption of raw material tax. (Review Opinion) The necessary foreign raw materials should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to verify that they are raw materials that cannot be produced domestically, compiled into a case, and reduced or exempted. The import tax should be discussed by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce with the competent authorities when revising the tax rules.

Case No. 90: Li Zuban, etc., proposes measures to address customs discrimination against national goods. Check the original case regarding foreign goods…after paying the full tax once…national goods…after paying the full tax one and a half times…If the abolition of transit tax is implemented, then the export tax from this port to that port and the re-import half tax should all be… included in the abolition of transit tax cases and should be handled accordingly. Before the abolition of transit tax is implemented, please resolve by the conference and request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities to first exempt the re-import half tax. As for the unequal treatment of Chinese and foreign goods mentioned in Items B, C, and D, please resolve by the conference and request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities and thoroughly investigate and revise them.

Proposal moved by the first group to earnestly implement the exchange law, strictly protect exchange tax revenue, and revise the exchange tax rate, that is, to use the increased tax revenue to handle basic cases. (Review Opinion) The original proposal still lists various methods, the main purpose of which is (1) to dispatch supervisors to crack down on improper profits of brokers and protect exchange revenue; (2) to revise the tax regulations of the exchange, not based on net profit but on total revenue calculated by total assets; and (3) to store the increased revenue in a special fund to establish industries. The exchange tax is still a legitimate source of tax revenue, and revitalizing industry is an urgent task at present. The methods listed in the original proposal seem feasible, and it is proposed to resolve by the conference and request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult with the competent authorities for review and implementation.

Case No. 20 moved by the fifth group proposes to clearly define firecrackers as not being superstitious items and to reduce the tax on their manufacturing raw materials. (Review Opinion) The proposed reduction in the tax on manufacturing firecracker raw materials refers to the currently levied saltpeter and sulfur tax in Guangdong Province. It should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities for review and handling.

Case No. 8 moved by the sixth group is the Industry Relief Case. The original proposal concerning this group has two points: (1) Exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous taxes should be eliminated; (2) Financial undertakings should be maintained. (Review Opinion) The first point should be included in the transit tax abolition case. The second point advocates that old public bonds should be reorganized and that internal debts that do not benefit production should not be issued in the future, which are insightful. It should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities to pay attention.

Case No. 9 moved by the sixth group proposes that the most important cases for industrial relief should first start with manual labor in silk reeling, cotton weaving, and silk weaving, and has drafted two methods for emergency relief and long-term solutions. (Review Opinion) Silk fabrics are heavily taxed with cocoon tax, silk tax, silk fabric tax, and product donations, which are truly the reasons for the decline of silk fabrics. For the various proposed methods, the tariff and commercial tax parts should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities to provide assistance. As for the terms and interest funds of the National Goods Bank loans, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce should determine the methods.

Case No. 11 moved by the sixth group is the urgent matter of commercial relief. The original proposal concerning this group has two points: (1) Public bond interest should not be too high, and tariffs should adopt protectionism. (Review Opinion) Both of the above points are insightful and should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities for appropriate handling.

Case No. 14 moved by the sixth group is the Industry Relief Case. (Review Opinion) The original proposal to reduce the tax rate on domestic cotton, cotton cloth, and foreign cotton so that daily necessities are not expensive is beneficial to people's livelihood and should be resolved by the conference and requested by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult the competent authorities for handling.

Case No. 21 moved by the sixth group is the relief of major industries such as silk, matches, flour, cigarettes, and silk weaving, which is divided into three items: (A) issuing relief public bonds, (B) reducing various tax rates, and (C) reducing transportation costs.

(Review Opinion) It should be resolved (A) by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, who should investigate and devise methods to implement it; (B) and (C) by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, who should consult the competent authorities for handling.

The Financial Affairs Section of the Fourth Group's Proposal on Industrial and Commercial Banks The original proposal was not received by August 20th, 1922. The case was re-submitted for review and reported that financial industries and industrial and commercial industries are interdependent. To develop industrial and commercial industries, it is impossible to succeed without establishing large-scale financial institutions. Therefore, the establishment of industrial and commercial banks is the current urgent need. The above-mentioned cases for establishing industrial and commercial banks list specific methods. It should be requested that the majority of the departments work together with the Ministry of Finance to adopt and implement them. However, before it is held, it should still be requested that the majority of the departments transfer the consulting to the Ministry of Finance, instructing the National Goods Bank and various banks to fully assist and organize warehouses to promote mortgage business, and order the banks to strictly prohibit speculation.

The Passage of Various Cases

Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau Should Exempt National Goods Advertising Tax 151

Zhou Dian finished the report and put it to discussion.

Zhang Zilian said that although the national goods advertising tax has already been submitted by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to the Executive Yuan to order the national tax exemption, the Shanghai Finance Bureau does not comply. Please ask the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to reissue an order for compliance. Also, regarding Case No. 80, reducing taxes on machinery that cannot be manufactured domestically will hinder the progress of imitation and should increase its tax.

The chairman said that this point can be submitted to the Tariff Committee for reference and attention. The chairman put the entire review report of the fourth group to a vote, and the majority passed it.

(Unnumbered) Regulations on rewarding domestic products

"Resolution": "Item 1" please the Ministry of Industry and Commerce handle as appropriate. "Items 2 and 3" handle according to the Special Industry Encouragement Law. "Item 4" please the Ministry of Industry and Commerce consult with the Ministry of Finance to handle the supplementary explanation "Proposal to establish a production craft guidance institution" (Chu Xiaoshi Huang Gong Huaiying) (Method) The central government establishes a production craft guidance bureau under the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Each province and city establishes a production craft guidance institute under the Department of Industry and Commerce, specializing in its affairs. (Organization) Divided into two departments: administrative and technical. The administrative aspect is divided into three sections: farmers' sideline craft section, pending craft section, and modern craft section. The technical aspect is staffed by people proficient in mechanical chemistry and art specialized craft talents and assisted by talents with special skills. As for the guiding steps, first start with farmers' existing handicrafts (such as textiles, cotton cloth, thread, rattan ropes, umbrellas, straw sandals, etc.), old-style inherent factories (such as porcelain, pottery, lacquerware, cloisonné, etc.), and new craft rudimentary factories (such as toys, stationery, printed silk cloth, clocks, etc.). Manual guidance and training will allow them to profit, and the general public will naturally imitate them, and then gradually expand the scope so that all production crafts can be established in sequence. Supplementary explanation Please the Ministry of Industry and Commerce consult the Ministry of Education or have industrial and commercial institutions raise funds to establish a craft vocational school (Chu Xiaoshi Huang Huaiying)

(Method) First establish craft vocational schools in the two education centers of Beijing and Ping, and attach practice factories and reference books that must be prepared first. Establish research departments within the school to train creative and inventive talents, and attach Class A schools and supplementary schools to popularize craft education and train talents at all levels. The subjects are temporarily divided into pottery, dyeing, printing, metalworking, woodwork, lacquer, precision machinery, patterns, etc. The above departments are currently lacking in industrial schools across the country, and these crafts are used daily and foreign goods are increasing. If measures are not taken to remedy this situation as soon as possible, there will be no day to maintain domestic goods and recover rights. (All of the above industries were resolved and passed)

Adoption of the Motion to Establish a Rayon Factory 159

The next discussion involved the Fifth Group's Cases 62 and 57 regarding the motion to establish a rayon factory, which was unanimously approved. The report is as follows: Upon investigation, the import of rayon has been extremely large recently, truly a major loss. People covet its smoothness and low price, and society has widely adopted it. Even natural silk fabrics cannot increase their price and benefit sales without being mixed with rayon. The people of the country are drinking poison to quench their thirst, which is undeniable. However, prohibiting imports is impossible. It is better to rise up and start manufacturing it ourselves in order to resist. It can be seen that those who proposed this motion have deep concern. However, the domestic silk industry is currently in a disastrous state. Now, advocating rayon seems like kicking our domestic natural silk when it is down. In fact, this is not the case. Because Chinese silk fabrics in today's society cannot survive without being mixed with rayon. We only need to make efforts to maintain and improve natural silk, making its quality and patterns increasingly exquisite. Then, there will be no time to export it in the future, so why worry about the status of our own country? Japan widely uses rayon, and at the same time, its natural silk still has made considerable progress. Now, it has defeated Chinese silk and holds the world's dominance, which can be further proof. Therefore, when reviewing this case,

Things can be changed to manufacture other types of medicines for military needs.

Industrial and commercial circles from all over the country were summoned to Beijing. Negatively, obstacles are removed; positively, incentives and promotions are emphasized. The plans were thorough, and the framework was clear. It is evident that our government has sincere intentions of nurturing and protecting industrial and commercial undertakings, and all gentlemen from all over the country have spared no effort to travel to the capital, expressing their candid views and jointly seeking construction. This is also sufficient to demonstrate the people's eager desire for governance. However, industrial and commercial undertakings are extremely complex. They rely on the government's maintenance and protection in various aspects, and they also rely on the unanimous efforts of the people of the country. At this time of military pacification and everything waiting to be rebuilt, promoting the development of industry and commerce, establishing an economic foundation, and consolidating peaceful unification are indeed urgent and cannot be delayed. The government's viewpoint of maintaining industrial and commercial undertakings is not only admired by the participating colleagues, but also the compass for industrial and commercial undertakings throughout the country. If the government can issue a clear order promulgating a policy to protect industry and commerce to be announced nationwide, the effectiveness of promoting the future development of industry and commerce will be even greater. Is it appropriate? Please wait for public decision. (Adopted)

Chairman Chiang Scheduled to Leave Ningbo Today 165

Lianjing Warship Steaming, Ready to Depart

Or Still Take the Xinningshao Steamer

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the National Government departed from Shanghai on the 24th of last month and returned to his hometown for a rest. It has been half a month. It was originally planned to go to Qingdao to meet with Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang and then return to Beijing to attend the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee. Now that Mr. Zhang will arrive directly in the capital ten days later, Mr. Chiang will no longer need to go to Qingdao. Yesterday, according to He Zhaoqing, the business director of the Xinningshao Steamer of Ningshao Company, the Lianjing warship sent to Ningbo to welcome Mr. Chiang has been steaming in the Ningbo River, ready to depart. Part of Mr. Chiang's guards have disembarked. It is expected that he will definitely leave Ningbo tomorrow (i.e., today). However, he may still take our steamer back to Shanghai because our steamer has greater power and less vibration, he said.

Agencies and Schools Hold Meetings

Must Follow the Rudiments of People's Rights 170

The Municipal Government Received an Order from the Executive Yuan Yesterday

Forwarded to Subordinates for Information and Compliance

The Municipal Government received an instruction from the Executive Yuan yesterday, saying: In order to comply with the order, the National Government's Instruction No. 577 stated: "The Central Executive Committee's Letter No. 16746 stated that training the people in the exercise of the four rights at the beginning of the period of political tutelage is the party's most important task today. The prerequisite for exercising the four rights is to make the people familiar with the rudiments of people's rights. All agencies, schools, and organizations should first be familiar with the rudiments of people's rights so that they can fulfill their responsibility to set an example for the people in exercising the four rights. Recently, it has been found that many agencies and schools under the government's rule have held various meetings that can follow the rudiments of people's rights, but there are also many that have not mastered the order and are chaotic, not only wasting time and reducing efficiency but also indirectly hindering the completion of the period of political tutelage. For this reason, in addition to notifying party departments at all levels to pay attention, a special letter is sent for your reference. It is hoped that all agencies and schools in the country will follow the rudiments of people's rights when holding meetings in order to train and achieve practical results." Therefore, we should comply. In addition to issuing orders and sending letters in reply, we hereby order your hospital to immediately comply and also instruct your subordinates to comply accordingly. It is heard that the instruction has been issued to the various bureaus under its jurisdiction for information.

The Municipal Government Vigorously Implements Local Autonomy

Yu Hongjun Appointed Concurrently as Director of the Local Autonomy Training Institute. The Municipal Government, considering Shanghai as a place where people from all walks of life gather and has a large population, believes that the most important task to uphold during the current period of political tutelage is to vigorously implement local autonomy so that it can start anew with the people and live up to the central government's efforts to govern. Since the promulgation of the Municipal Organization Law on May 28 of this year, it has been working hard on the foundation to promote it step by step and see its success as soon as possible. The Municipal Government has divided the original 17 districts of South Shanghai, Zhabei, Yinxiang, Yangjing, Pusong, Tangqiao, Fahua, Yangsi, Caojing, Luxing, Gaohang, Wusong, Yinxing, Jiangwan, Pengpu, Gaoqiao, and Zhenru, according to the latest population statistics totaling 355,648 households, into districts, neighborhoods, and lanes as stipulated by the Municipal Organization Law, and established a Municipal District Division Committee to implement the district division work. It has also divided them into general affairs and investigation groups to be responsible for statistics, mapping, and investigation matters and will delineate autonomous regions in the shortest possible time. The Municipal Government also considers cultivating talents as the fundamental plan for handling local autonomy. Now that the district division work is about to be completed and the autonomous organs should begin to be set up, all candidates below the district chief before the elected district chief is realized must have considerable knowledge and ability to be competent and happy. Therefore, at the beginning of the district division work, it simultaneously prepared to set up a local autonomy personnel training institute, and the organizational preparatory committee actively prepared to train autonomous talents below the district chief. Each term enrolls 200 students, divided into two classes: a special class for those with local autonomy experience, who will be issued lectures by the institute to study on their own and will be gathered for regular examinations; and an ordinary class for those who have been admitted to the institute for training, both with a three-month training period, teaching the Premier's will, the outline of local autonomy, the outline of municipal administration, the outline of social science, and the outline of statistics. After the end of the term, the graduates will be tested, and those who pass will be assigned to various district autonomous organs for three months of practice, and those who pass the best of the grades will be awarded certificates, and those who fail will be ordered to make up their studies. Now, preparations are gradually being made for the institute. Yesterday, the Municipal Government specially appointed Secretary Yu Hongjun to be the director of the institute and ordered him to open it quickly in order to cultivate autonomous talents, he said.

Said There is a New Plan to Suppress the Communist Bandits. The Handling of the Lu Department Still Awaits Detailed Discussion of Measures.

Zhang Zhen, Commander of the newly organized First Division, is scheduled to take a car to Beijing this morning with Secretary Lin Peiran and others. I have drafted a new plan for thoroughly suppressing them, which can be decided after meeting with Chairman Chiang. In short, the handling of the Lu department will be decided after careful consultation by all parties, he said.

The Local News Censorship Has Not Yet Been Ordered to Be Cancelled

Talk by a Staff Member of the Censorship Office 171

Yesterday's newspaper reported that the Central Standing Committee has resolved to end the anti-rebellion military affairs and stop news censorship. Propaganda Minister Liu Luyin also talked about stopping news censorship immediately. This reporter went to the News Censorship Office yesterday to inquire about when the local news censorship will be cancelled. According to the staff member of the office, news censorship is a work of hard work and dedication. Due to the different subjective positions of individuals and the differences in positions, newspapers must record everything they hear and strive to publish as much news as possible. Censors, on the other hand, are cautious in their work and strive to avoid mistakes. Therefore, there are times when newspapers and the censorship office have different views, which is unavoidable. All colleagues in this office are willing to be relieved of this duty as soon as possible. The Garrison Headquarters telegraphed the Headquarters last year to ask whether the censorship could be cancelled. With the end of this war, Commander Xiong again presented it to the Headquarters for cancellation. Because whether to cancel it or not, the Central Government needs to make a whole discussion, not limited to Shanghai, so the approval has not yet been received, nor has any order been received. The Garrison Headquarters

The News Censorship Office was established by order of Commander-in-Chief Chiang two years ago. As soon as a cancellation order is received, the censorship will be stopped immediately, he said.

Liu Zhi Telephonically Requests Expedited Delivery of Pay for the 20th Route Army 178

Jiangnan Provincial Government Chairman Liu Zhi urgently telegraphed Commander-in-Chief Chiang on the 31st of last month, requesting the swift dispatch of pay for the troops under the command of Zhang Fang, Commander-in-Chief of the 20th Route Army. An excerpt of the telegram is as follows: Urgent delivery is required; no delays are permitted along the way. Addressed to Commander-in-Chief Chiang at Fenghua: I, your subordinate, have thoroughly investigated the matter. Since the various units under the command of Commander-in-Chief Zhang Fang of the 20th Route Army were successively formed in August, September, and October, the pay received has been meager, with each soldier receiving only three or four yuan, totaling less than one month's worth. I am well aware of their immense hardship. The units in southern Henan have been reorganized into one division and three brigades by Director He. The units in western Henan have not yet been fully inspected. However, the sustenance for these divisions has not been disbursed for a long time, and the provision of cotton clothing is also lacking. Currently, the weather is cold, and the soldiers lack clothing and food, suffering from hunger and cold. If assistance is not provided promptly, it will be difficult for the starving troops to endure. I earnestly request that you instruct the management office to swiftly disburse the clothing and food expenses for the one division and three brigades in southern Henan, and also provide funds for the ongoing maintenance of the units in western Henan to alleviate their immediate crisis. The route army urgently needs 50,000 sets of cotton military clothing. Due to the continuous rain and cold weather, further delays are unacceptable. I earnestly request that they be dispatched in full and transported to Henan day and night for distribution. This matter concerns the suffering of the route army and the security of the region, so I dare to report it directly. I await your instructions on how to proceed. Your subordinate, Liu Zhi, respectfully bows. World Seal.

Canada's Harsh Treatment of Overseas Chinese

A Letter from the Vancouver Chinese Benevolent Association

Please Seriously Negotiate with the Canadian Trade Mission

The Vancouver Chinese Benevolent Association of Canada sent a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: We are writing to inform you that Canadian merchants are visiting China, hoping to seize our country's commercial rights. We respectfully request that your chamber take this opportunity to tell the Canadian merchants about the injustices of the Canadian people's harsh treatment of our overseas Chinese. The National Chamber of Commerce of Canada has selected fifty Canadian merchants to travel together to China. They set sail from this port on the 16th of October aboard the Canadian Pacific Company's Empress of Russia, landing in Japan first and then arriving in Shanghai, scheduled to arrive at the port on the 10th of November. Their declared aim is to promote friendly relations between Chinese and Canadian businessmen, but their real purpose is to introduce Canadian goods and sell them in our country, with timber, wheat, grains, fish, and milk being the main items. Trade and commerce are recognized as legitimate actions by all countries today, which is originally nothing strange. However, the Canadians seek to sell Canadian goods in China, absorbing our people's wealth and resources, not hesitating to travel thousands of miles, lowering their heads and humbling themselves to please our people. At the same time, the Canadians in their own country, officials and civilians alike, regard finding ways to harshly treat Chinese overseas Chinese as their only important task. Even bureaucrats and politicians often use anti-Chinese policies as a shortcut to advancement, resulting in an endless stream of anti-Chinese regulations that are constantly updated. Since the Canadian government implemented the 43 harsh immigration regulations against China on June 30, 1923, all types of Chinese people other than Chinese government personnel have been refused entry into Canada. Also, for example, the constitution of British Columbia does not allow Chinese people born in the country the right to vote. Their intention is to prevent Chinese people born in the country from having the right to vote. If they find out that someone usually advocates anti-Chinese policies, they will reject him when it comes to elections, and not elect him, because they want to get a majority of the votes, so they have something to worry about and dare not advocate anti-Chinese policies. Another example is the regulations to ban agricultural produce markets, the minimum wage regulations, the regulations to limit the working hours of workers, the factory inspection regulations, and the case of restricting overseas Chinese from hiring Western women to work. The above-mentioned harsh regulations are specifically designed for our overseas Chinese. This is the main point, clearly revealed. Other minor details are nitpicking, and the harshness is countless. Our overseas Chinese are bound and oppressed by various harsh regulations and are suffering every day. They are in a state of upside-down waiting for relief. Now, taking advantage of the opportunity of Canadian merchants coming to China to seek friendly relations between China and Canada, we humbly request that your chamber, when meeting with these merchants, bring up the cruel methods of the Canadians' harsh treatment of overseas Chinese, which greatly violate humanity and disregard justice, and tell them, hoping that they will return to their country and promote and explain to their people, realize something, abolish the harsh regulations, and adopt a treaty of equal treatment in commerce. We have always admired your esteemed chamber's concern for overseas Chinese and your unwavering attention to them, and we will be happy to rescue overseas Chinese from fire and water and put them on the agenda. We are truly grateful for your kindness. Sincerely, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

Wuhu Chamber of Commerce Requests Extension for Closing Accounts

Set the End Date as February 15th of the Following Year 181

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday received a letter from the Wuhu General Chamber of Commerce. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce: Since our chamber received the government's announcement of the implementation of the national calendar last year, we immediately notified all businesses to comply. Since summer, there has been no objection. However, the rampant bandits have been rampant for years, and the harvests in the past five years have not been good. This year's wheat season was poor, and rice was scarce and expensive. The launch of peace and industry has been depressed, and financial resources have been blocked. The summer festival's collection of accounts has not been completed. Although this year we were fortunate enough to have an autumn harvest, the grain prices hurt farmers, and financial resources are still sluggish. The autumn festival's collection of accounts is less than 20%. If the accounts of the two festivals are like this, then the collection of accounts for the New Year will definitely not be completed on time. Moreover, the period at the end of December is very close to the end of September. Agricultural products have not yet been converted into money to pay off debts. How can the accounts of stores be closed? Since the accounts of stores cannot be closed, how can the funds used by Wuhu money houses be settled? If one party only knows to abide by the closing date and strictly urge the payment of debts, and the debtors cannot comply, they will inevitably sue to the law. A single hair moves the whole body. Not only will there be endless disputes in Wuhu stores, I am afraid that the places involved in wholesale accounts will also be overturned. Stores and money houses will suffer the same harm. We cannot but take care of both sides. Yesterday, the joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees decided to invoke Executive Yuan Order No. 4158 of the 18th year to postpone the New Year's closing of accounts by one month to provide relief. After the New Year's holiday, stores will only collect debts and not release debts. At that time, agricultural products have entered the market, and financial activity will be limited for one month. The accounts can be completed. In addition to submitting reports to the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the Anhui Provincial Government for filing, we should also telegraph to inquire and hope that you will immediately notify your city's banks and money houses that all Wuhu's annual accounts will end on February 15th of the following year to avoid squeezing and achieve dual benefits. Sincerely, Wuhu General Chamber of Commerce to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. After receiving the letter, the city has notified both the Silver and Money Houses.

Telegraphic News of the Mishap of the Japanese Ship Hakusan Maru

Shanghai Passengers Have All Landed

Now Grounded on a Shoal in Kobe Unloading Cargo

The Japanese Mail Company's European liner Hakusan Maru is the company's first-class mail ship with a net registered tonnage of 13,350 tons. This time, it was returning to Japan from Europe via Shanghai. Unexpectedly, on its way from Shanghai to Japan, it had a collision accident in Kobe. One passenger also died. The news received by the company yesterday is as follows:

Collision Situation: It was found that the Hakusan Maru left Shanghai on the 4th and was heading to the 3rd Pier of the Hatoba Promontory in Kobe at 3:35 PM on the 6th. It happened that the Norwegian freighter Denmark (net registered tonnage 5,500 tons) was departing from Kobe. When the two ships were approaching, the water was turbulent and the wind was strong, making it impossible for them to give way to each other. As a result, the bow of the Denmark struck the waist of the Hakusan Maru. Fortunately, the captain of the Hakusan Maru, Kato Michi, quickly reversed and retreated, avoiding being cut in two. However, a large hole had been punched in the outer hull of the coal bunker, and seawater flooded into the cabin. The Hakusan Maru immediately tilted towards the sea, almost capsizing. The captain urgently ordered the ship to run aground on a shoal to maintain the hull.

Passengers Rescued: The impact force was extremely strong at the time of the collision. There were many passengers on board traveling from Europe to Japan. Passengers disembarking in Japan from Shanghai included Chen Zhengye, Wu Lianshan, Fang Guoyun, Ye Wanxing, and Japanese nationals Tongguchi Ito, Saito, and Moyu, a total of ten people. They rushed to the deck trying to escape. A 68-year-old British priest fell and died on the ship. The captain ordered the sailors to first release small boats and carry all the passengers on board, large and small, ashore. At that time, the ship was half tilted and people could not stand on the sea surface. Yesterday afternoon, the local port received a telegram stating that all the passengers on board had been rescued safely. Everyone praised it.

Rescue Situation: After this incident occurred, the captain telegraphed the head office for help. The company dispatched more than ten iron barges and small boats to the scene. First, the mail and important cargo were unloaded. The Kobe Customs also sent a small boat to the scene of the accident to assist and protect the ships. The company is now planning to extract as much of the cargo as possible and then tow the ship into the shipyard for major repairs. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the Shanghai office received a telegram from the head office stating that the dangerous period for the ship had passed, but the cargo in each cabin had suffered considerable water damage.

Notice to Passengers: Yesterday afternoon, the Shanghai branch immediately issued a notice stating that the Hakusan Maru had collided with the Denmark in Kobe, and all passengers had been rescued without injury. Repair work is now underway. The ship was originally scheduled to depart on its 18th voyage to Europe next month on the 15th. Now, it is impossible to make a decision and the trip will be vacant. Passengers who have booked seats on the ship have been instructed to take the Hazuna Maru to Europe instead.

Responsibility Question: The question of responsibility for this collision between the two ships is still unclear at the moment. It must be investigated on the spot together with the Denmark side before it can be determined. The bow of the Denmark was also damaged, while the damage to the hull of the Hakusan Maru, the water damage to the cargo, and the losses due to the missed voyage are very large, amounting to at least hundreds of thousands of yuan.

Su Bo Lie Fu Returns to Shanghai after Cycling Around the World

Su Bo Lie Fu Returns to Shanghai 183

Departed from Shanghai Two Years Ago

Welcomed by the Russian Youth Association

Russian youth Su Bo Lie Fu, who set off from Shanghai two years ago, has returned to Shanghai after successfully completing his journey around the world by bicycle, traversing three continents and traveling more than 34,000 miles. He arrived in port yesterday aboard the Nagasaki Maru from Japan. When Mr. Su set off, he only carried a few photos, a set of clothes, and twenty yuan in silver. After arriving in Hong Kong and Bangkok, he was fortunate enough to receive assistance from local people, who gave him a new bicycle, allowing him to continue his journey. He then traveled through India, England, and various European countries before crossing the ocean to America and traversing the American continent. Now, he has returned to Shanghai from America. The local Youth Association specially sent representatives to the pier to welcome him and held a meeting at the association's headquarters at 311 Hualong Road to celebrate his success.

According to Mr. Su, he left Shanghai with his bicycle on November 7th of the previous year. After arriving in Hong Kong by boat, his travel expenses ran out and difficulties arose due to his nationality. Fortunately, a Norwegian shipowner took pity on him and offered him a free ride to Bangkok, the capital of Siam. However, at that time, his funds were exhausted and he was almost like a fish stranded in a dry rut. Fortunately, the British press in Bangkok provided assistance, allowing him to continue his journey. Mr. Li Anjun of Bangkok even gave him a new bicycle, which was even more timely. At that time, a certain young overseas Chinese also had grand ambitions and was riding his bicycle together. Unfortunately, he was bitten by a snake a few hours after departure and died. Mr. Su was fortunate enough to escape unharmed. Afterwards, he continued to travel alone, spending 24 days in the wilderness of Siam. He relied solely on coconuts and milk for food and drink. The bread and clean water he carried had long been used up. The people along the way treated him very well. When he arrived at the Straits Settlements border, the British refused him entry and sent him back to Bangkok by train. Later, the British Consul in Bangkok made an exception and gave him an entry permit, allowing him to re-enter the Straits Settlements. From Penang to Singapore, he traveled 508 miles in five days. After arriving in Singapore, he used the money he earned from selling photos along the way to buy a motorized bicycle and traveled with a German companion towards Rangoon. Before long, the German encountered danger and returned. Mr. Su continued to travel alone to Burma, passing through Rangoon to Butwan to see its chief. He then passed through Bombay and Delhi and arrived in Lahore. After the Afghan authorities refused him entry, he decided to pass through Ben Ze Bai and traveled 787 kilometers across the desert in 16 days to reach Karachi. He was favored by the local British officials and given a new motorized bicycle. He then entered Persia and was shot at by Kurdish bandits, but managed to escape by driving fast, fortunately without injury. He then passed through Tehran to Baghdad, crossed the Arabian Desert, and arrived at Dama Yi. This was the most difficult part of the whole journey. After arriving in Dama Yi, he continued to Palestine. In Jerusalem, he visited the 103-year-old Greek Orthodox Church bishop and was presented with a Jesus cross. He then went to Jaffa and took a boat to France, landing in Marseille. From there, he went to Rome via Paris, entered Yugoslavia

He then went to see King Alexander I. Then he turned back to the northwest and visited Dr. Eckener in Germany, who presented him with a Graf Zeppelin commemorative medal. Then he went to Belgium and then to England. The British treated him very well and he was given free food and lodging in a hotel, as well as a boat ticket to the United States. In the United States, he passed through New York, Washington, Chicago, Los Angeles, San Francisco, and Seattle before entering Vancouver, Canada. He then took a boat back to Shanghai via Japan, passing through twenty countries and traveling more than 34,000 miles.

Principal of Zhongshan Public School in Makassar Expelled and Sent Back to China 184

Dutch Authorities Suppress Party Affairs Propaganda

Treat Overseas Chinese with Extreme Harshness

(Huadong News Agency) Feng Han Yue, the principal of Zhongshan Public School in Makassar, Nanyang, was originally sent by Ding Weifen, the training minister of the Central Party Department, to reorganize the overseas Chinese education in Nanyang. Mr. Feng went to the Netherlands in February of last year and has been there for a year and a half. He has spared no effort in reorganizing overseas Chinese education. As a result, the number of students in the school, which originally had only more than 130 students, has now increased to more than 300. While he was working hard to reorganize, he unexpectedly suffered the jealousy of the local Dutch authorities. The Dutch authorities have always strictly suppressed Chinese in the Netherlands, and especially hated propaganda related to party affairs. Since Zhongshan Public School is presided over by the branch of the Kuomintang stationed in the area, the authorities have been constantly vigilant against the school. If there is a minor incident, Mr. Feng will be summoned for questioning. In total, he was

summoned more than thirty times this year. On September 27, Mr. Feng was suddenly detained by the local authorities and then ordered to be deported back to China. Mr. Feng had no choice but to stumble back to his country and arrived in Shanghai a few days ago. According to Mr. Feng, the Dutch authorities' actions towards Chinese are extremely harsh and outrageous.

Some are experts, some are famous locals, and all are very knowledgeable in gardening, especially in chrysanthemum cultivation. The reporter went to visit yesterday. A couplet was hung at the entrance of the field, which read: "Rely on a good time for the exhibition, it is good to be idle and quiet, and have less fun; take advantage of the chrysanthemum festival and discuss how to promote the urbanization of the city and the countryside." Entering the gate, there are winding streams and corridors, bamboo forests, and rocks stacked to form a mountain. The mountain has a small pond with a sprinkler tube and goldfish. The rocks on the mountain are decorated with chrysanthemums, and green potted plants are mixed in between, adding a unique elegance. There are two extremely high chrysanthemum mountains in the courtyard, one woven from yellow chrysanthemums to form the four characters of the Three Principles of the People, and the other stacked into a character shape, demonstrating the propaganda of the doctrine and the ingenuity of the layout. The flower rooms and greenhouses in the field are newly built this year. The mounds are cultivated into mounds at the Songgou winding, and a thatched pavilion is built on top. Climbing up, you can overlook the ferry across the Huangpu River. Mr. Zhu Futian plans to build a small pavilion here to climb and overlook, this move of the field is to commemorate the predecessors and to fulfill Mr. Zhu's unfinished ambition. At the secluded place of the exhibition, a special refined room is opened to display pens and ink, and dozens of pages of jade paper and ruler pages decorated with porcelain green are named Juying Hongti, which means that they want to get the poems of poets, recluses, famous scholars, and painters, and leave traces of snow and mud.

Sentencing in the 100,000 Yuan Robbery Case

Zhu Desheng and Others Imprisoned for Fourteen Years 188

On August 28 of this year, Hangzhou Zhejiang Local Bank instructed Wang Weiqun and others to transport 200,000 yuan to the Huadong Lai Bank. On the way, at the intersection of North Henan Road and Tiantong Road, 100,000 yuan was stolen. Subsequently, Hua Inspector You Agen, Officer Song Bingzheng, Cui Chengke, Liu Junqing, and Sergeant Huang Fusen of the Lao Zha Police Station arrested the master thieves Zhu Cheng (aka Desheng), Liang Houbiao, Wang E, Wang Yang, He Guoshengcheng, and eleven others in this case on the 30th of that month. They were sent to the Special District Court. After the interrogation was completed, they waited for the sentencing. The circumstances of the case have been repeatedly recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou Hanting and Prosecutor Xu Mei were seated in the First Criminal Court and announced the sentence. Zhu Desheng, Wang E, and Wang Yang were each sentenced to 14 years of imprisonment for the crime of jointly committing robbery. Liang Houbiao was sentenced to 12 years of imprisonment for the crime of jointly committing robbery. Sheng Cheng and He Guo were sentenced to 8 years of imprisonment each for the same crime. The number of days of detention before the judgment is confirmed shall be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. The money and green silk, etc., that were recovered were given to Liang Dingchang, Hua Wangshi, Liang Lvshi, He Xiangquan, and He Xushi. All were found not guilty. The police lawyer Ru Bao Yi declared that he would not appeal for the defendants who were declared not guilty and were released in court.

Ni Xiuzhen sues Zhu Haisheng

On Grounds of Luring and Abandonment 190

Ms. Ni Xiuzhen, a woman residing at No. 108, Hongqing Lane, Xin Zha Road, recently hired lawyer Gu Jirong to sue Zhu Haisheng, a foreman at the Rui Rong Iron Factory in Yangshupu, for crimes of luring and abandonment, among others, at the Special District Court. The main points of her complaint are as follows: The plaintiff's father passed away early, and she lived with her mother. In March of the sixteenth year of the Republic (when she was only seventeen years old), Zhu Haisheng lured her in every possible way, forcibly engaging in ambiguous cohabitation, falsely claiming to be unmarried and vowing lifelong commitment. The plaintiff, young and naive, was ultimately violated and then lived with him at No. 9 Qingdao Road. Last year, she gave birth to a child who died within a few months. The plaintiff, based on the defendant's prior promises, urged him to quickly complete the marriage ceremony. The defendant repeatedly used excuses such as not having raised enough money, but the defendant’s monthly expenses were eighty yuan. The plaintiff treated him with utmost care as if he were sincere, causing her to delay for more than two years. Unexpectedly, in December of this year, the defendant became increasingly distant, cutting off the monthly allowance and eventually disappearing from the plaintiff's residence. After much investigation, it was discovered that the defendant had built another home on Huade Road, in Shende Lane, abandoning the old for the new and forgetting to return. When the plaintiff demanded living expenses, she was beaten. The plaintiff cried and complained, but her mother, Ms. Qian, was also at a loss. Attempts to reason with the defendant were also rejected, leaving the plaintiff in a dilemma, unable to become a wife and without a way to support herself, feeling a sense of hopelessness. Nothing in the world is more cruel than this. Considering that the plaintiff is a young and weak girl with an unstable will, mistakenly trusting a scoundrel and being abused in this way, even though it can be said that the calamity was self-inflicted, what else can be said? But the plaintiff's future is bleak, with no hope for the future. How can this be tolerated by natural justice, human emotions, law, and morality? Therefore, she petitions the court to sentence him under Article 257 of the criminal law for enticing a woman under twenty years of age to leave the guardianship of a person with parental rights, and to award her alimony of five thousand yuan. Yesterday, Judge Cheng Shangfeng held a court session to collect testimony. As a result, the court ordered a postponement of one week for further interrogation. The defendant, Zhu Haisheng, was absent due to being out of town. Lawyer Ye Kang appeared in court on his behalf, stating that the plaintiff's accusation under Article 257 of the criminal law was inappropriate. The plaintiff, Ni Xiuzhen, and her mother appeared in court, stating that she has a mother, a younger brother, and a grandmother. Zhu lured her, and after giving birth to a child, Zhu neglected her, hence the lawsuit. Judge Cheng asked Ms. Xiuzhen's mother a few questions and then ordered a postponement to summon Zhu Haisheng for further questioning.

Judgment in the Old Fire Stove Case 194

Chen Laijin from Suzhou, Liu Jiajun from Anhui, and Ren Heibao from Nanjing were making noise and beating Liu Yukang at the old fire stove run by Liu Yukang at No. 805, Pingliang Road, around 4:00 PM the day before. Liu reported to the nearby patrolling police officers Nos. 2438 and 1940 that they were extorting him for twenty yuan. The two Chinese constables arrested Chen, Liu, and Ren together and took them to the Yangshupu Police Station. Five yuan in banknotes were found on Chen. The police chief ordered their detention. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the Special District Court. Zhang Tianyin, a lawyer from the police station, stated that the case originated from a seven-year-old child from Wuxi, a neighbor of the old fire stove, who went to the plaintiff to get water and started crying after being beaten. His mother went to negotiate, and they argued with each other. The defendants, dissatisfied, also beat the plaintiff. The police station is now charging the defendants with assault, as there is insufficient evidence of extortion. Then, the plaintiff Liu Yukang testified that the three defendants extorted twenty yuan and slapped and punched him. Yang Luo also testified that she sent her young son Yongxing to the plaintiff to get water, but he was beaten and cried. She then went to reason with him and was slapped, kicked, and verbally abused. Therefore, the three neighboring defendants felt injustice and negotiated with him. The testimony of the three defendants was the same as hers, and there was no mention of extorting money. Judge Ge Zhiqin examined the statements and ruled that Chen Laijin, Liu Jiajun, and Ren Heibao would each be fined twenty yuan as a warning.

The Great Lord Cheats and Kills

Absurdly Claims That Doctors in the Human World Are Useless

Callously Watches an Old Woman Die

You Shen, a 63-year-old woman from Suzhou residing at No. 147, Sande Lane, Chenjiabang, is usually devout in her Buddhist faith, worshipping Buddha and respecting gods. Her son, You Runsheng, works as a clerk in a foreign firm and is very filial to his mother. She suddenly suffered from asthma and coughing last month, unable to sleep at night. Her son urgently hired Chinese and Western doctors for diagnosis, but she was too old and weak, and the treatments were ineffective. She superstitiously consulted a male witch from Suzhou residing on Meierjin Road, who claimed to be the "Great Lord of Suzhou." He said that she was haunted by tuberculosis ghosts and afflicted by the Iron Snake and White Tiger constellations and needed to invite more than a dozen Taoist priests to perform rituals to ward off evil spirits, including a packet of incense ashes and a bowl of sacred water, instructing her to sincerely drink them, saying that earthly doctors were useless and that she should rely solely on the Great Lord's treatment, which would reduce her illness by half in three days. Believing this to be true, she and the male witch agreed to invite Taoist priests to perform rituals for three days, including warding off evil spirits, offering sacrifices to heaven, at a cost of sixty-two yuan. The male witch came to her house once a day, charging six yuan eight jiao each visit. Her son burned incense day and night, sincerely asking the Great Lord to heal his mother's illness. However, the Taoist priests performed rituals in the male witch's house, in front of the Great Lord's altar, with loud gongs and drums, from the 5th to yesterday (the 7th), three days of rituals were completed. However, after refusing treatment from Chinese and Western doctors and drinking the sacred water and incense ashes, her condition worsened day by day. Yesterday evening, as the male witch led the Taoist priests to her house to thank the kitchen god and see off the spirits, she died at that moment. The whole family cried loudly. Seeing that things were not going well, the male witch took the opportunity to leave with the Taoist priests without even completing the ritual. The harm of superstition is evident here.
