This Year's Business Conditions on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway

Revenue of More Than Seven Million in Seven Months 198

The Shanghai-Nanjing Railway has always had more developed passenger and freight transport revenue than the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway because the Shanghai-Nanjing line is longer, runs through more large cities, and is the main route to and from the capital. In recent years, revenue has increased even further. Last year, the total annual operating revenue reached 12,039,881.9 yuan. This year is even better than last year. From January to July of this year, total operating revenue has already reached 7,008,806.7 yuan. Compared to the revenue from January to July last year, this year's revenue has increased by 87,830 yuan. It is expected that the year-end settlement this year will exceed last year's results.

Continued Report on Foreign Ship Seamen Demanding Pay Raise 199

Dockworkers Demand Pay Raise; Chinese Seamen on Foreign Ships Demand a Pay Raise Following the Example of Chinese Ships. Negotiations on the case of Chinese seamen on foreign ships demanding increased wages, following the precedent of Chinese ships, have been ongoing for a long time and are about to reach a conclusion. However, the salaries of the dockworkers on each ship are extremely low and have not increased in recent years. Taking advantage of the seamen's pay raise, they also submitted a request to the Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, and Nissin shipping companies to increase their wages across the board. The Seamen's Union is also representing them in this request. Yesterday, the Union received a reply from Taikoo stating that the dockworkers are hired by the Chinese compradors and have nothing to do with the company. In the past, the company gave the Chinese compradors 100 taels of silver per ship for the dockworkers' wages, but now it has increased to 500 taels. The Union believes that since the compradors have increased their income, the dockworkers' wages should also be increased, which is very unreasonable. Union committee members Tang Hesheng, Lu Yongzhi, Ma Zhongxian, and others, representing the dockworkers, went to Shanghai yesterday to contact Mr. Chen, the comprador of the Taikoo Yangtze River ship Poyang, and asked him to increase the wages of the dockworkers. Chen had just left work and came to Shanghai to discuss a raise. The comprador of the Huangpu ship also heard this news and quickly offered to increase the wages by one or two yuan. However, the dockworkers did not agree and insisted on a six-yuan increase across the board. The dockworkers on the Jardine Matheson and Nissin ships have also unanimously started demanding an increase.

Small Dispute Over Seamen's Pay Raise; Taikoo has signed a contract with the labor side regarding the seamen's pay raise, but in the contract, Taikoo only agreed to increase the wages starting in November. The seamen's side requested that the increase start in September. Special Union representative Wang Yongsheng consulted with mediator Yu Qiaqing at Sanbei. Yu said that this matter can be resolved satisfactorily. However, the contract also included the phrase "no more pay raises forever," which the seamen opposed. They requested that this phrase be removed, otherwise, the seamen's side would have to add the phrase "another pay raise in March of next year" to counter it. Yu agreed to discuss this.

Preparatory Meeting for Dredging the Yu Pond 200

The Shanghai County Yu Pond Dredging Preparatory Committee held its eighth preparatory meeting at 2:00 PM on the 6th at the Beiqiao Third District Office. Chairman Yang Fulin passed the following resolutions: (1) Discuss the proposal to change the course of the North Bay section of the Qian Pond outlet to the Jinjia River. It was resolved that, based on water conservancy considerations, the channel should be straightened and diverted to the Jinjia River, and the committee should submit separate reports to the county bureau for record. (2) Discuss when to start dredging the Yu Pond. It was resolved to start building the dam on November 30th. (3) Discuss how to raise funds for the dredging expenses before the collection is completed. It was resolved to request the county government to instruct the Finance Bureau to advance 5,000 yuan first, and the remaining amount will be raised separately by each district. (4) Discuss whether the committee should be terminated on a regular basis and whether a river works committee should be established to take charge. It was resolved that a river works committee should be organized in accordance with Article 10 of the Provisional Regulations for Dredging Rivers in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province, and that the committee should be terminated after the river works committee is established. (5) Discuss how the river works committee should be established. It was resolved that the committee should notify the relevant districts to elect reputable individuals as members of the river works committee and report to the committee by the 10th of this month for submission to the county government for record. (6) Discuss when the river works committee should be established. It was decided that the inaugural meeting would be held at 10:00 AM on the 13th of this month at the Third District Office.

The Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Plans to Build a Freight Yard at Ganlu Port

The Railway Bureau Submits a Request to the Ministry of Railways for Approval 201

Gentry and merchants in Gaozi Township, Zhenjiang, recognized that the river channel next to the freight yard at the Zhenjiang Jiangbian Station was becoming increasingly silted, and despite repeated dredging, there was no significant improvement, making it difficult to load and unload goods. The China Foreign Famine Relief Committee Discusses Relief Work in Henan 205

The Shanghai China Foreign Famine Relief Committee received a report from the Kaifeng Henan China Foreign Famine Relief Committee on November 2, which is transcribed as follows: "Since Henan Province has been plagued by drought, locusts, hail, and bandits in recent years, the people have suffered beyond endurance. This spring, war clouds suddenly arose, pervading the Central Plains, and countless people have died in the rain of bullets and artillery fire. Now, after the ravages of war, fertile fields have been transformed into ditches, and huts have been turned into mounds. The displaced refugees have no homes to return to and no land to cultivate. The tragic situation of displacement cannot be fully described even by the Zheng Xia map. Witnessing this suffering, our committee is deeply saddened and urgently seeks to provide relief. The most serious disaster is in eastern Henan. After discussion, it was decided to allocate 30,000 yuan from the committee's existing funds to build the Kaiyong highway to provide relief through work. However, this route only passes through a few counties and does not cover even one-tenth of the disaster area, making it difficult to extend the relief efforts. We have long admired your committee's assistance and enthusiastic commitment to Henan relief. Therefore, we have entrusted our chairman, Liu Hailou, to go to Shanghai to present the details and appeal for help. We have recently received a telegram from Chairman Liu stating that he has already met with your honorable office and that you have shown great concern for the disaster in Henan. He has asked us to formally submit a letter describing the relief measures so that they can be submitted to the meeting. The disaster situation in Henan is difficult to describe. The war in eastern Henan, the natural disasters in western Henan, the banditry in southern Henan, and the defeated soldiers in northern Henan have all contributed to a catastrophe that has not been seen in centuries. There is no way to reverse the situation or provide effective relief. As winter approaches, the dying survivors have no choice but to turn to ditches for shelter. Our committee currently plans to start relief work in the relatively stable areas and is organizing relief through work, including the Kaiyong Road, as well as the Kaixu, Kaikao, and Kaizhou roads, which are all in the war zone. If we can continue to repair these roads, the disaster victims can make a living. However, the project is huge and beyond our capabilities, and the work relief only reaches able-bodied men, leaving the elderly and weak in need of assistance. Therefore, urgent relief measures such as soup kitchens and flat boats should also be planned and maintained. A cup of water can hardly put out a cartload of burning firewood. If your committee can provide strong assistance and allocate funds for the project, then we will gratefully lead the millions of disaster victims in Henan Province to bow our heads and pray." It is heard that the committee believes that, given the cold weather and the fact that the entire province of Henan has been turned into a disaster area with countless people facing starvation, the above plans and winter relief are extremely appropriate and have been submitted to the relief division for discussion in the hope of early implementation.

Responses to the Xiao Case 206

The Yixing Alumni Association Sends a Telegram to Jiangwan Road, Shanghai Law School: The Yixing Alumni Association of Shanghai Law School sent a telegram yesterday to various newspaper offices and the National Government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which reads: "Ms. Xiao Xin'an, a native of our hometown, was invited to teach at the Peide School on Anbon Island in the Dutch East Indies. On the way, she was forcibly raped by the first and second mates of the Java Company's ship. This barbaric act is not only a disgrace to Ms. Xiao personally, but also a disgrace to the entire Chinese nation. Moreover, it is not only a national disgrace but is being used as a tool of Dutch imperialism, treating our people as cattle and horses to be arbitrarily trampled upon. This is not merely a personal matter but a major issue concerning the rise and fall of our national dignity. We humbly request your ministry to base its actions on public opinion and lodge a serious protest. Not yielding to power or letting emotions lead us astray, ensure that the Dutch who despise our nation's barbaric acts are turned into morning dew on the execution ground. Then, our nation may still have the qualification to survive in the world with dignity. If not, how can your ministry face the people of the country, and how can you face the nations of the world? The honor and disgrace of our nation depend on this one action. May Zhang Guoyan emphasize national humiliation and send an urgent telegram filled with grief. Yixing Alumni Association of Shanghai Law School, Yu."

Citizens of Harbin Send a Telegram to the Overseas Chinese Federation: The Overseas Chinese Federation received a telegram from Cheng Ying and more than forty other citizens of Harbin, which reads: "Having read the reports and learned of the outrage in your telegram regarding the rape of female teacher Xiao Xin'an by the first and second mates of the Java Company's ship "Zhibade," we are filled with righteous indignation. If the first and second mates are not given the most severe punishment, how can we deter others in the future and how can we wash away this shame? Ms. Xiao, as a weak woman, is under the pressure of the Dutch. Having been falsely accused, she cannot live and cannot die, satisfying the lust of the first and second mates and bringing shame to our entire nation. Who does not have sisters or families? If we do not provide assistance to Ms. Xiao, how can we ensure that our own sisters, wives, and daughters will not be treated the same as Ms. Xiao, as instruments of pleasure for the Dutch? All our compatriots should immediately implement the federation's proposal to sever all ties with the company, not travel on the company's ships, not ship goods on the company's ships, and not post advertisements on the company's ships, as well as their import and export news. At the same time, we should petition the government to lodge a serious protest, demanding that the Dutch government severely punish the first and second mates and issue a formal apology to our government. The people here will fully support your federation. The telegram is sent with utmost indignation."

The Seamen's General Union Sends a Telegram: "Xiao Xin'an, a woman, is a citizen of China and a teacher in our culture. Her origin is so great, her status is so high, and her body is so precious and dignified. Yet, she was seduced by the Dutch first and second mates of the Java Company's ship "Zhibade," and when they failed, they raped her. They even dared to strangle her neck and poke her chest, strip her pants and force her to die. Afterwards, the ship's doctor even fabricated a story about her being mentally ill to cover up their crime. This is all because they rely on the power of their imperialism to bully our great country, China, thinking that there is no one to stop them. Therefore, they dare to indulge their lust, commit rape and murder, and then spread rumors and arbitrarily slander her. Nothing in the world is more tragic than this, and no injustice is more unjust than this. If we allow such people to go unpunished, I fear that this trend will continue, and all our virtuous and dignified women who travel by sea for a living will be like meat on the chopping block, fish in a pot. The system and prestige of our Republic of China will also be swept away. All of us Chinese people, sisters of the same Chinese Han race, and those who have been oppressed and trampled upon by imperialists and their running dogs, now witness her shame and pain, and are forced to commit suicide. How can we not be filled with grief and come forward to help? The club is taking revenge for Miss Xiao and considering the reputation of our China. In addition to formally submitting a serious protest to the central government and sending personnel to announce a boycott of the company's ships and seamen, we dare to send a telegram to the whole country, respectfully requesting that all circles unite to strive for a victory and must put forward the following conditions: (1) Legally handle the rape and injury of the first mate, etc. (2) Compensate Miss Xiao for her reputation, medical expenses, etc. (3) The government of the country concerned must formally apologize to our national government and declare that such incidents must not happen again in the future. The club is willing to lead the entire 800,000 seamen to act as vanguards, striving to achieve the goal of victory before. With utmost indignation and pain, I respectfully look forward to your wise judgment. The Organizing Committee of the Chinese Seamen's Industrial Federation pays homage."

Bandits and Rogues

All Expelled from the French Concession 207

Repeated Robberies: Cai Shaoxuan, nicknamed "Little Guangdong," specialized in colluding with accomplices to rob pedestrians of their belongings in the French Concession. French Police Detective Gao Xinfa discovered and apprehended Cai. Interrogated at the police station, Cai confessed to robbing pedestrians Zhu Hongbin, Cao Axiu, Hua Jingcai, Sun Bingsheng, and dancer Cao Yuanming, totaling five individuals, of silver dollars, clothing, and other items. He did not deny using foreign currency. Chief Detective Lun ordered Cai to be detained. Yesterday, escorted by the plaintiffs, Cai was brought before the French court.

The plaintiffs recounted the circumstances of the robberies. Cai admitted to the robberies without hesitation. Chinese and Western judges sentenced Cai Shaoxuan to five years in a Western prison, after which he would be permanently expelled from the French Concession.

Impersonating an Inspector: The rogue Song Qingxiang, on the evening before last, near Route Paul Beau in the French Concession, impersonated an inspector, attempting to rob pedestrian Sun Hongzhen of his belongings. A Western detective from the French Police happened to pass by, apprehended Song, and brought him to the police station. Yesterday, Song was brought before the French court. Plaintiff Sun Hongzhen stated that he was passing through the area that night when the defendant ordered him to stop and be inspected. The Western detective arrived, discovered the ruse, and made the arrest. He requested an investigation. Song Qingxiang confessed to impersonating an inspector and attempting to rob the victim. Chinese and Western judges sentenced Song to three months in a Western prison, after which he would be permanently expelled from the French Concession.

Cruel Treatment of a Young Girl Leads to One-Year Sentence 208

Chen Lin, residing at No. 4, Zhufu Lane, Qiujiang Road, in the Chinese area, had her 13-year-old niece, Mei Bao, introduced by Christian missionary Zhang Li to Cao Qiu, a fellow Christian at No. 1, Puqing Lane, Route Massenet in the French Concession, to learn how to make foreign socks. However, Cao Qiu subjected Mei Bao to all kinds of abuse, leading to her death from beatings. French Police Detective discovered the incident, arrested Cao Qiu, and brought her before the French court. After preliminary interrogation, the court ordered a later hearing. Yesterday, the hearing resumed. Witnesses Zhu Jingqing, Wang Shuofu, Liu Zhaoquan, and Gu Zhu testified that they were living with Cao Qiu and often heard sounds of beatings and Mei Bao crying. They did not witness the beatings. The Head Western Detective reported that a Western doctor had confirmed Mei Bao's death was due to beatings. He requested a verdict. Cao Qiu admitted to minor reprimands, but otherwise evaded the questioning. The Chinese and Western judges ruled that the evidence proved Cao Qiu's guilt and sentenced her to one year in a women's prison as a warning to others.

Robbery on Gordon Road Last Night 209

At approximately 10:15 PM last night, six robbers broke into No. 1153 Gordon Road. Four carried axes, one held a knife, and one wielded an iron bar, threatening the homeowner into silence. They ransacked the place, stealing $400 in banknotes and foreign currency before fleeing with loud cries. The homeowner reported the incident to the local police station, requesting an investigation and arrest.

The funeral of Mr. Wu Linshu, a giant in the local cotton industry, is scheduled for tomorrow (the 9th). Nanjing Road, in particular, is usually not permitted for funeral processions. The coffin of Mr. Zhu Baosan once passed through it in the fifteenth year of the Republic. This time, at the request of Mr. Feng Bingnan, the Municipal Council made an exception to express its respect and admiration for Mr. Wu.

Li Xiaonan's Memorial Service Tomorrow 217

Mr. Li Xiaonan was a prominent member of the Revolutionary Party. At the end of the Qing Dynasty, when he was seventeen, he joined the Tongmenghui (Revolutionary Alliance) while studying at the Anhui Military Academy and was responsible for military work in Anhui. He participated in several uprisings with martyr Ni Yingdian and martyr Xiong Chengji. During the Xinhai Revolution, he served as the temporary commander, leading troops to declare independence. He was appointed as the commander of the First Brigade of Anhui. After 1913, he participated in the campaign against Yuan Shikai to uphold the Provisional Constitution. In the sixteenth year of the Republic, during the Northern Expedition, he served as the commander of the Fourth Division of the Thirty-third Army. After the split between Ning and Han, he retired from military service and returned to Shanghai. Recently, feeling the difficulties of the times, he closed his doors and recuperated, passing away on March 18th this spring. His family has chosen November 9th to hold a memorial service at the Puji Temple at the intersection of Route Lafayett and Rue P. Froc. Fellow Anhui natives and comrades, in memory of Mr. Li's revolutionary spirit and achievements, have launched a public memorial service.

Commercial Magazine Participates in "Reading Movement" 218

The Commercial Magazine, published by the Commercial Magazine Company at the Central Building on Sichuan Road, Shanghai, has been considered the only reading material for businessmen and industrial researchers for many years due to its rich content and excellent printing. It has been widely welcomed and distributed throughout the country. The "Reading Movement" initiated by the Chinese Youth Association on Sichuan Road opened the day before yesterday (the 6th), with over ten thousand visitors. The magazine company has displayed all the magazines it has published over the years. The Youth Association recognizes the value of this magazine and has allowed them to set up a display area at the entrance of the Grand Hall for public viewing. Special prices are available for on-site purchases, truly a boon for readers.

Xie Liheng's Message to Shanghai's Chinese Medicine Community 220

Xie Liheng, Standing Committee Member of the Shanghai Chinese Medicine Association, Addresses Shanghai's Central District:

A public notice to the Shanghai Chinese Medicine community: The Shanghai Chinese Medicine Association was jointly organized by the China Medical Union, the China National Medical Association, and the Shanghai Chinese Medicine Society to unite Chinese medicine practitioners in the city and protect their professional interests. Now, the People's Training Committee has ordered the merger of the three medical groups into the Association, clarifying that disunity should be replaced by unity, which is in line with the initial intent of combining the various medical groups. Unexpectedly, the leaders of the medical groups have responded by publishing notices to withdraw from the Association. If there are deficiencies in the Association's content and management, you should work together to rectify them, eliminate the bad and preserve the good, so that the Association can develop further. If everyone engages in withdrawing from the Association and undermining its foundation, then the hard work of combining in recent years will be in vain. Not only will the thousands of registered Chinese medicine practitioners in Shanghai lose legal protection, but it will also increase ridicule from the outside world. I personally believe that this is inappropriate. I hope you will consider this carefully, safeguard the overall situation, and enable the Chinese medicine community to have a formal and positive unity, so that we can progress in our careers. This is what I hope for.

Farewell Banquet for Tan Zhen, Going to Japan 221

Mr. Tan Zhen, the secretary of Minister of Interior Niu Yongjian, is going to Japan to study politics and economics. Former classmates from Beijing Police College and Shanghai Agricultural School, as well as the printing industry and Xinxin Company, held a farewell banquet at the Atlantic Restaurant on Fourth Avenue last night. Over twenty people attended, including Chen Ya-fu, Kang Tongyi, Qiu Yunming, Zhang Youren, Wu Hongsheng, and Chen Xi. After some rounds of drinks, Mr. Chen Ya-fu gave a speech, saying that Mr. Tan has been working for the revolution for many years and has made contributions to the Party and the country. This trip to Japan is to further his studies. It is predicted that after completing his studies and returning to China, he will make a further contribution to the society. He raised his glass to wish him a safe journey and unlimited prospects. Mr. Qiu, Mr. Zhang, and others followed with speeches. Finally, Mr. Tan gave a speech, briefly stating the purpose of going to Japan to study and thanking everyone for their kindness.

News from Labor Unions 224

The Candle Industry Reorganization Committee convened a board meeting yesterday, chaired by Chen Zenghao. Resolutions: (1) Standing Director Chen Zenghao, due to difficulties in handling affairs, sent a letter of resignation. It was resolved to persuade him to stay. (2) The Candle Industry Association sent a letter rejecting the proposed wage increase. It was resolved to send Chen Zenghao, Shen Jinrong, and Yang Ashui as representatives of the committee to negotiate. (3) Wan Tai newly hired non-union members. It was resolved to send personnel to negotiate.

The Cantonese Cuisine Restaurant and Teahouse Workers' Union convened its thirteenth executive committee meeting yesterday, chaired by Liang Yonggu. Opening remarks and agenda (abridged). Discussion items: (A) How to commemorate Sun Yat-sen's birthday. It was resolved to send representatives to participate in the commemoration, notify workers to work as usual, and send a letter to employers requesting double wages. (B) Should the lack of resolution for past savings be reported to all levels of government for investigation? It was resolved to report for investigation. (C) How should personnel within the scope of the union who have not joined but are working be handled? It was resolved to send a letter to employers to prioritize hiring union members and not deliberately undermining the union, and to warn non-union workers that if they deliberately resist, the union will report to higher authorities for sanctions. (D) Fan Zhengbo and Zhu Yingpeng sent a letter recommending the purchase of Hanli Company's Zhong Ying printing machine to promote national goods. It was resolved to ask Chen Feng to explain the details of the printing machine and then have him explain all matters related to the printing machine research. A test printing of the four characters "共同奮鬥" (Common Struggle) was very convenient, and applause erupted. The meeting then adjourned.

The Preparatory Committee of the Cigarette Industry Workers' Federation held its twelfth standing committee meeting yesterday. Chairman Gu Ruofeng reported (abridged). (1) It was resolved to approve the request from the Hexing Workers' Union, proposed by the Standing Committee, to forward a petition for approval. (2) It was resolved to submit a request to the Municipal Training Committee for instructions on whether to allow the organization of workers in this industry who are not yet organized, as the Social Affairs Bureau's standards for organizing labor unions have been established. Other matters omitted.

The Seamen's Branch held its fourteenth standing committee meeting yesterday. Chairman Wang Yongsheng convened the meeting and resolved the following: (1) The General Association's instruction to submit a list of the heads of the three departments that does not match the original case and to issue a form for re-investigation and filling out shall be followed. (2) The General Association's instruction that the Seamen's Association logo should be affixed to the committee member's oath shall be followed. (3) The General Association's instruction that those in charge of the case of the New Daming disaster-stricken workers should go to the General Association to await consultation and be handled accordingly was resolved to be carried out by sending Committee Member Lu Yin to the General Association on Monday morning. (4) The Stevedore Association requested that the preaching of reactionary partisans on ships should be stopped. It was resolved to refer this matter to the Secretariat for handling. (5) The Jiang'an wheel's mid-cabin unit reported that a re-election of the group has been requested for the record. It was resolved to convene the group leader to a meeting for discussion. Discussion items: (1) Worker Han Tingyu of the Datong wheel was unjustly dismissed and requested reinstatement. It was resolved to send Cao Shanren to investigate. (2) The New Taikoo Stevedore Club requested a six-dollar raise per person. Please immediately write to the business director of each wheel to arrange the raise. It was resolved to approve the request. Provisional motions: (1) The Yihai Stevedore Club nominated a director and requested approval. It was resolved to approve after the majority of sponsors from each wheel hold a meeting. (2) Wang Furong reported that Zhu Quanhong has reduced wages and requested serious negotiation. It was resolved to forward a request to the General Association to be submitted to the Central Government for investigation. (3) Chuan Rongfang, a mid-cabin worker on the Emei wheel, requested reinstatement. It was resolved to review the case when the ship arrives.

The Coal and Fuel Workers' Union convened an executive committee meeting yesterday, chaired by Zhang Xiaoyang. Resolutions: (1) On the issue of the proposed five-cent wage increase, a majority in Hongkou have not yet complied. How should this be handled? It was resolved to wait for written reports from members before submitting to higher authorities for handling. (2) Recently, coal companies have been forcing workers to sign special agreements that impede union affairs. How should this be addressed? It was resolved that in addition to notifying all workers to unanimously oppose the agreements, letters should be sent to the Coal Association and individual coal companies not to use these agreements in order to maintain labor rights. (3) Workers at the Zhonghua Coal Briquette Company have not paid union dues. It was resolved to send a letter of advice. If they intentionally do not pay, the matter will be reported to higher authorities for handling. (4) Regulations for Fee Collectors Remitting Payments: It was resolved that each person, regardless of the amount collected, must remit payment to the accounting office on the same day and must not use it for private purposes. When departing to collect fees, each person will be issued two dimes for food expenses by the union. (5) Date for Salary Payments for Union Staff: It was resolved that salaries will be paid every month on the third day of each ten-day period. (6) The number of unemployed members is increasing. How should this be handled? It was resolved to send a letter to the Coal Industry Association for handling.

Free Talk

A Word or Two 227

— Qiushui

Men under thirty often waste valuable time engaging in reckless and foolish acts. Between thirty and fifty, they try to repent. After fifty, they boast about the things they did in their youth, praising themselves incessantly.

If men could clearly express a precise and unchangeable standard for women, human life would be simpler, sweeter, and more peaceful.

A woman is an animal that digs to the root and is good at asking questions. If she gets the answer "yes" from a boyfriend to the question of whether he loves her, she will ask him why he loves her. Men either win or lose at this point.

Women often like to ask men questions and interrogate them for reasons, but men are most afraid of being questioned, and their actions are often unreasonable. There seems to be a natural contradiction between the two. However, love between men and women does not diminish because of this. There is an incredible magic in it.

When a child is building a wall out of mud and stones, he does not want anyone to help him, or he will lose the fun. Similarly, when a man falls in love with a woman, he does not want anyone to help him.

Men are like cats. As long as you let them be free and comfortable, they will sometimes obey you very faithfully. Women are like dogs. As long as you constantly play with them and give them things to eat, they will obey you very docilely.

A man can lose the last hair on his head, his last friend, and his last dollar. However, unless his last enthusiasm is lost, the fire in his heart will never be extinguished.

"Why did you get married?" Nine out of ten men cannot answer this simple question, and nine out of ten women refuse to answer it.

Cibei Education Circle's Bicycle Race 228

— Jieyu

The teaching staff of over twenty schools, including Cibei Xianzheng, Qiu Shi, and Jintang, jointly organized a bicycle race in the foothills of Mount Fulong. A friend sent a letter describing the small details of the event, which are excerpted below.

The White-Haired Judges: Several judges were invited, all prominent figures in the county. On the day of the race, Mr. Weng Ruiqing from Minghe was publicly elected as the chairman of the judges. Mr. Weng is old and his beard and eyebrows are white, and he is gradually balding. However, he still mustered his energy to judge fairly, showing that his enthusiasm for sports has not diminished with age.

The Mountain Road is Steep and Difficult: The contestants usually practice on the flat and expansive playground, which is easy to ride. Unexpectedly, the race location was set on the steep and difficult Mount Fulong. Thorns blocked the way, and gravel obstructed the wheels. The riders bounced and leaped, not only causing pain in their buttocks, but also causing them to fall and bleed.

Elementary School Student Wins the Championship: Shao, a fourth-grade student at Jintang School, is only fourteen years old. He lives near the foothills of Mount Fulong. This time, he participated in the race with a team of thirty people. Few were able to reach halfway up the mountain. Only Shao was familiar with the mountain, so it was fitting that he won the championship.

Female Teachers are Afraid of Difficulties: Two or three female teachers also intended to show off their skills. However, when they saw the path, they immediately became afraid of the difficulties and canceled their participation, returning in disappointment.

Remembering Zhang Yu's Wedding 229

— Zhao Dingming

Mr. Zhang Peiyi, also known as Zhenhou, is skilled in photography. He and his associates Hu Boxiang and Lang Jingshan founded Huashe, the only photography organization famous at home and abroad, and organized with Mr. Guo Xiqi, Wang Dafo, Zhu Shouren, Hu Bozhou, and others. On November 1st, at the Zhenxin Club in Zhenxin Lane, Dongxin Bridge, South Shanghai, he celebrated the marriage of his talented son, Yingchao. Mr. Yingchao likes photography, calligraphy, and painting, and is especially good at sculpture, a budding artist. The bride, Ms. Yu Liying, is good at poetry. She studied at Zhirenyong Girls' School and was known as a female poet.

At eleven o'clock, I and Mr. Hu Bozhou went to congratulate them. Looking around the four walls, we saw congratulatory scrolls and silk banners everywhere. The ink calligraphy and congratulatory couplets sent by Wang Yiting, Zhang Shanzi, Xu Yongqing, Hu Boxiang, Jiang Xiaojian, Yang Qingjing, Fang Xuegu, and other painters, writers, and photographers were the most elegant and refined. The stone sculpture of Cupid presented by the artist Zhang Chenbo was the most precious.

At twelve o'clock, Ms. Zhou Hufeng, Ms. Lang Lei Peizhi, and Mrs. Wang Dafo arrived in droves. Congratulatory guests poured through the door. Subsequently, more than forty foreign male and female guests arrived one after another. Mr. Zhenhou shook hands with them one by one, with the utmost courtesy. The foreign guests also expressed their congratulations. Yingchao saw this and rushed forward to shake hands and bow. He bowed hastily to the newly arrived relatives and friends. The Western women laughed out loud when they saw this, which was due to the difference in Chinese and Western etiquette. However, it was also because Yingchao was tall and bowed 120 degrees to everyone, which easily attracted attention.

At three o'clock in the afternoon, the wedding ceremony began with the sound of drums and music. The bride, Ms. Yu Liying, was exquisite, petite, graceful, and beautiful. Her height only reached the groom's chest. The guests were surprised because the bride and groom were both nineteen years old and their birthdays were only five days apart. Mr. Shen Lianfang officiated the wedding. Mr. Xie Zhonghe and Mr. Pan Digong were the introducers, and Mr. Li Changjue was the master of ceremonies, all filled with joy. First, the officiant gave a speech, followed by congratulatory speeches from the guests. Mr. Yan Duhe and Mr. Zhou Shoujuan gave speeches that were extremely humorous and witty. The ceremony was completed at four o'clock.

Cheng Yanqiu and Chen Liqing 230

— Ji Chuan

Shi Nai'an's *Water Margin* is a supremely excellent work under heaven, and Jin Shengtan long ago included it in his list of books for talented scholars. However, strictly speaking, the latter half is somewhat lax compared to the concise and moving first few dozen chapters. Yu Zhonghua of Shanyin wrote *The Pacification of Bandits*, and many ridiculed him for being like a mantis trying to stop a chariot, overestimating himself. Yet, the first half of his work, depicting the personality and behavior of Chen Liqing, establishes a unique style beyond the 108 heroes of the former book, making the reader feel as if a charming and lively young woman is about to leap from the pages. The meticulous planning, careful management, layout, and writing are all masterful, the crystallization of the author's efforts. I have often said that *Water Margin* encompasses countless Beijing operas and Kunqu operas, a natural source of material for playwrights. The first half of *The Pacification of Bandits*, before the establishment of the Yuanbi stronghold, is also excellent dramatic material. The veteran performer Yu Yuqin (i.e., Yu She) once staged *The Pacification of Bandits*, starting from "Strolling Through the Temple" and ending with "Anle Village." The scene of burning and looting Anle Village was particularly intense and lively, especially the fighting scenes, which were superb. She was once praised as "Female Changpo." Recently, Yanqiu has been rehearsing *Chen Liqing*, based on Yuqin's version but with revisions and insertions, truly perfecting it. The main part, from the father-daughter argument to escaping from Tokyo, is slightly different from Yuqin's version. The role of Chen Liqing in this play is extremely difficult to portray. She is sometimes rebellious and sometimes… it is necessary to hold fast to the three qualities of (ingenuousness), (heroism), and (chivalry). Her obedience and submissiveness to Chen Xizhen, revealing the natural bond and true feelings between father and daughter, is greatly beneficial to the world and people's hearts today. Her affected manners and forced smiles towards Gao Yanei are entirely depicted in reverse, to emphasize the venom of the arrow pavilion beating the horse. Her ability to hit the target with one shot revitalizes the audience. Yanqiu has pondered this play for a long time and is comfortable and skillful with it. However, she is unwilling to show it lightly and has never performed it even in ordinary times. It is said that rehearsals are underway and it will soon be staged. Those who love watching Yanqiu's plays must not miss it, and those who enjoy reading *The Pacification of Bandits* should especially not miss it.

Editorial Department of Free Talk.

Impressions of West Lake (II) 231

— Huijian

From the Broken Bridge, I boarded a boat, passing along Bai Causeway and through the Brocade Belt Bridge, venturing into the Outer Lake and temporarily anchoring at Gushan. From Baoshi Mountain, I captured a scene with Baochu Pagoda at its center. The setting sun bathed the mountain in colors like rose quartz, and the northwestern part was ablaze with vibrant clouds. The beauty of the evening scene is beyond the power of words to describe. After admiring it for a long time, the boatman urged me to depart, so we proceeded west along Gushan, passing the Crane Release Pavilion, Lin Hejing's Tomb, and Feng Xiaoqing's Tomb, stopping at Xiling Bridge. We went ashore to visit Su Xiao's Tomb. A lone pavilion, adorned with vulgar couplets, offered nothing of interest. Next to it was Wu Song's Tomb, repaired by Tu Minshi, oval in shape and bearing a stele inscribed with the names of Huang, Zhang, and Du from Shanghai. A marker was carved on the tomb stating, "Wu Song's spirit never dies," which everyone found amusing. Further on was Qiu Jin's Tomb, a Western-style structure built ten years ago. I had often heard that Su Manshu's tomb was also located here, but despite searching everywhere, I could not find it. I asked the boatman and Banxia, but they were both bewildered and unable to answer. I lingered by the roadside, lost in thought, forgetting where I was. Banxia, Lao Lan, and others urged me to leave, so we slowly made our way to Yue Temple. Looking at my watch, it was almost 6:00 PM.

Entering Yue Temple, I was pleased to find that the visitors had mostly dispersed as it was getting late. The guard was about to lock the gates, but after offering him two small silver dollars, he happily agreed to be our guide. In the main hall, a few candles were still burning. Passing through the hall, we entered Qizhong Shrine and reached Yue Fei's Tomb. By then, it was completely dark, and the trees rustled in the evening mist, creating a desolate and lonely atmosphere. While inspecting the iron statues of Qin Hui and his wife, Banxia jokingly remarked that Qin's wife's drooping breasts showed the beauty of ancient sculpture. Everyone chuckled. Upon exiting Yue Temple, children were hawking scented beads of various qualities, claiming they came from Taizhou, and some were even using nanmu to pass off as sandalwood. I bought a few strings; the price was very low. We then boarded the boat again and sailed from Yue Temple back to the front of Gushan. By then, the lights were ablaze, and a silvery-white full moon rose in the east. The scene on the lake became even more serene and tranquil. We proceeded slowly along the southern shore of Gushan, passing Yu Lou (Yu Quyuan's villa), and went ashore for dinner. West Lake is famous for its sweet and sour fish and water shield soup, but I found it rather mediocre. Perhaps the choice of restaurant was not ideal.

After dinner, we boarded the boat again and turned south, reaching Three Pools Mirroring the Moon. Under the cool moon, the candlelights illuminated the water, and the rising mist filled the lake with an ethereal light. The boats on the lake, slender as bamboo leaves, were rowed swiftly back and forth by two oarsmen like water birds. I lay back and looked at the sky, unknowingly falling asleep. Lao Lan shook me awake, and we had reached Three Pools Mirroring the Moon. As it was the Mid-Autumn Festival that evening, there were hundreds of boats, and the teahouses on the pools hung large gasoline lamps, their bright lights dimming the moonlight. The three pagodas in the pools were originally hollow structures made of stone. The locals pasted red and green paper on the stones and placed a candle inside, so from a distance, they looked like paper lanterns. Lao Lan, seeing this for the first time, insisted on touching them as a souvenir. We went ashore beside the pools, sat and drank tea for a while, but felt the night air was too chilly to bear. Banxia, slightly drunk and dizzy, also expressed a desire to return. So, we asked the boatman to take us back to the eastern shore. Far from the pools, the bustling market could no longer be heard. "Floating clouds in the eternal cold, the moon filling the boat," Banxia recited poetically. I gazed at the moon, lost in thought, savoring the beauty of West Lake.

European Travelogue (84)

— Liu Haisu

Diary of a Tour in Italy

(III) Ten Days in Rome (IV)

Day Two: The Colosseum, the Arch of Constantine, the Baths of Caracalla, and the Catacombs. On the second day, after much hesitation, we visited the Colosseum, the largest remaining building in the world and a relic of the era of Emperor Titus of Rome.

Under the scorching sun, gazing at the Colosseum, looming against the blue sky, it truly resembled a giant skull. The layers of dilapidated arches looked like the holes in a skull. Anyone who saw it would wonder why such a strange structure was built. I never imagined that the Roman Colosseum would have such a grand and austere appearance. Although it was covered in wounds, with beams broken and walls collapsed, far from its original state, recalling the history of the most cruel gladiatorial contests and the tragic deaths of Christians filled me with a chilling dread.

Emperor Titus built this theater, capable of holding tens of thousands of people, eighteen hundred and several decades ago. Now it has become a desolate ruin. Walking inside, hundreds of layers of mottled and broken stone steps are densely arranged, stretching to the towering peak. Looking down, many cellars are scattered below, some deep and some shallow. These were once the places where ferocious beasts were kept. I imagined the scene of lions, tigers, and other beasts leaping out of these cellars to attack people, and I involuntarily shivered.

Greek art did not provide the Romans with a precedent for this type of arched structure. Although the Hellenized East understood arches, they did not use them in such large buildings. The Colosseum's arches were unprecedented. The walls and arches were seamlessly connected, without any trace of division. Each arch was decorated with stone statues, giving the entire structure a sense of stability. Unfortunately, many of these carvings have now been destroyed, and the remaining ones have been moved to various museums. The Colosseum is the first large building in Rome that has been preserved to this day. This architectural method was both economical and fast. Such a large Colosseum only took ten years to build. However, this also created many shortcomings. Later architects criticized it for being merely a decorative facade, which is why it could not last for a long time. However, architects of the Renaissance also intentionally followed this path.

Built near the Colosseum, standing majestically among the lush green trees, is a mottled white stone arch, showing a purely Greek style of bas-relief, entering our field of vision. This is the Arch of Constantine, built by Emperor Constantine in the early fourth century after his victory over Maxence. It is the largest triumphal arch in Rome, and it became the object of worship for all artists, painters, and sculptors during the Renaissance. The composition of its bas-reliefs and the symmetry of its lines are truly the forerunners of modern painting. These seemingly difficult-to-distinguish white bas-reliefs, appearing and disappearing in the ruins, have become the only building in the history of Roman sculpture that has been admired by later generations, bearing an eternal life.

New York, 6th of the month: The American Cotton Receiving Office's estimate for the current year's new cotton production is 14,574,000 bales, an increase of 115,020 bales compared to the previous estimate (October 6th). Grain and Rice Market: Rising Trend Intensifies

Top Grade Japonica Reaches 16.30 Yuan 240

Yesterday, fewer than ten boats arrived at Zhabei, and sales were brisk. Due to the limited supply of new japonica rice and continuous rain, sales were especially strong, and prices rose sharply by 0.60-0.70 yuan. Top grade rice reached 16.23 yuan. Thin-husked rice also followed, rising by 0.30 yuan. Customers inquired about Yangxian rice, with prices opening high at 13.80 yuan, up 0.40 yuan. The supply of Du Jian rice is gradually decreasing, with prices rising by 0.50 yuan. Top grade rice reached the 14 yuan mark. Local Xian rice prices also rose by about 0.30 yuan. Top grade rice was priced at 13.20 yuan. All day, both japonica and xian rice were eagerly purchased by various customers.

This caused sellers to arbitrarily increase prices, further driving up prices. Baiyuan rice also increased by 0.40-0.50 yuan, with the highest price reaching 16.50 yuan. Diao Pi (inferior) rice was also very active.

Yesterday in Shanghai South, only six or seven boats arrived from inland areas, and business was extremely brisk. Prices for new japonica rice from Changbang continued to rise, with top grade rice opening at 15 yuan, an increase of 0.30-0.40 yuan, reflecting the shortage of top grade japonica rice in this area. Suzhou Tong japonica rice sales were quite strong, with various parties rushing to purchase it, and top grade rice reached around 14 yuan. Southern early thin-husked rice was universally rising in price. Yongshao stores, retail sales, and customer sales were all actively purchasing, and demand exceeded supply. Prices were expected to rise by 0.50 yuan, reaching as high as 15.30 yuan. The buying interest for Du Jian rice was active, and prices also tightened by 0.30 yuan, with top grade rice opening above the 13 yuan mark. The market for Yangxian rice was extremely tight, with top grade rice opening at 12.50 yuan. Bianyuan rice remained quiet, with prices gradually increasing by 0.20-0.30 yuan, opening high at 15.23 yuan.

Foreign Rice Follows Du Rice Upward 241

Yesterday, the arrival of customer Xian rice was not high, and sales were excellent. The market did not see any improvement, and various types of machine-milled Xian rice continued to rise by 0.05-0.12 yuan. Jiangxi machine-milled early rice opened at 2,000 bags, handled by the Xiamen gang. The local market focused on foreign rice, with not much Xian rice being handled. The Tianjin gang handled over 200 bags of Hunan machine-milled Yuan rice, priced at 15 yuan. Jiangxi machine-milled early top grade rice opened at 11.25-11 yuan, and middle grade rice opened at 10.09-10.06 yuan, even more popular than top grade rice. Anqing machine-milled rice opened at 140 bags, priced at 10.055 yuan. Nanjing machine-milled rice opened at over 400 bags, priced at 10.085-10.095 yuan.

The inventory of foreign rice is not large, and it has been selling well for some time. However, yesterday, due to the increase in Du rice by 0.50 yuan, middle to lower grade Xian rice rose by 0.10-0.12 yuan. The local market frequently focused on rice, with a total of over 40 bags being sold at retail prices of 0 yuan and wholesale prices, priced at 10.065-10.055 yuan, also an increase of 0.15 yuan compared to the previous day.

Flour Market Turns Favorable

Short Sellers Compete to Cover... Inland Gang Absorbs 242

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, market sentiment for various months was not as weak as before due to better quotations for foreign wheat, with differences of 0.20-0.30 yuan. The current month's spot goods from factories, such as standard flour, still require 0.30 yuan, and medium-grade brands also require 0.27-0.28 yuan. Mama brand, due to its particularly high quality, still opened at 0.33-0.34 yuan. Therefore, realistically speaking, standard flour has fallen to its lowest price, which is unacceptable to customers. The dissatisfaction of customers is that the factories failed to consider the usual practice of not allowing cash withdrawals, which prevented standard flour from establishing itself. Throughout the day, due to short sellers competing to cover and absorption by the inland gang, market sentiment returned to favorable. However, future gains and losses still depend on the factories' attitude. As a result, the current month increased by 0.015 yuan compared to the previous day, December increased by 0.0175 yuan, January increased by 0.025 yuan, February and March increased by 0.02, and April increased by 0.0175 yuan.

Wheat Market Shows Slight Rebound 243

Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market in the morning and afternoon, various months showed a firm trend. Due to better quotations for foreign wheat, with differences of 0.20-0.30 yuan, both bulls and bears were quiet. However, after the large drop, a portion of the short sellers actively covered. Furthermore, with the market falling to this level, neither bulls nor bears have a clear target to pursue. Their direction is based on the overall environment. If flour sales become more active in the future, the wheat market may show a slight rebound. As a result, the current month increased by 0.04 yuan compared to the previous day, December increased by 0.03 yuan, January and February increased by 0.04 yuan, March increased by 0.03 yuan, and April increased by 0.02 yuan. The spot wheat market for top grade goods remains quiet, while medium to lower grade transactions are still stable. Factories handled over 1,800 bags, and over 3,000 bags of Xianghe Hankou wheat remained in the hands of merchants.

Exploring the Reasons for the Plunge in the White Tung Oil Market 247

Since the autumn, the white tung oil market has repeatedly fallen to the lowest price in more than a decade. The reasons are approximately three: (1) Overseas competition has led to a sharp decrease in exports. The United States is the largest importer of our country's tung oil. In the first half of this year, only 5,987,000 pounds were exported to the United States, a huge difference compared to the 46,635,000 pounds in the same period last year. Only 1,465,000 pounds were exported to Europe. (2) Because Hunan, the main tung oil producing area in our country, has had a bumper grain harvest and rice prices have plummeted, villagers who used to hoard tung seeds are now storing grain in anticipation of better prices. All tung seeds in the producing areas are being dumped on the market, and the market is flooded with spot goods. (3) Domestic sales are weak. The war in North China has just ended, and the area is devastated, so there is no possibility of development. Various gangs in Jiangsu and Zhejiang also prefer to use Hongyou because it is cheaper, leading to an imbalance between supply and demand, which is why the market has plummeted.

Art Circle

Sinclair Lewis 267

— Translated by Xie Fulan

1930 Nobel Prize for Literature Winner

On the 5th of this month, Reuters sent a telegram from the capital of Sweden telling us that the 1930 Nobel Prize for Literature was awarded to American novelist Sinclair Lewis. The amount of this prize is a total of 6,500 British pounds, which, calculated at the current exchange rate, is worth about 120,000 Chinese dollars.

Sinclair Lewis is a famous satirical novelist. In his works, he categorizes Americans into many types, and once people are assessed by him, it feels undeniably accurate. Although he published a "Main Street,"

Relying on this later novel, he used his cruel pen to describe the psychology of small towns with subtle accuracy, thus gaining prominence in the modern literary world.

Following "Main Street," he published "Babbitt" in 1922. Since this book was published, it has created a new term for those who live on the track of contented success. His satirical mark on humanity, in modern American terms, is akin to blasphemy. Five years later, he published another book, "Elmer Gantry," which was tantamount to hitting the clergy head-on. Every minister and evangelist was slandered by this book with scathing criticism, but his most valuable contribution to literature may be "Arrowsmith," published in 1925.

This is a story about scientific effort and struggle. In this, Sinclair Lewis does not expose the follies and weaknesses of scientists, but pays a sincere tribute to their work and life. In addition, works such as "The Man Who Knew Coolidge," "Man Trap," and "Dodsworth" are also widely circulated.

Sinclair Lewis was born in 1885 in a small town in Minnesota, USA. He graduated from Yale University in 1907 with a Bachelor of Arts degree and worked as a reporter for a newspaper. After that, he successively accepted invitations from "New Haven Journal & Courier," "San Francisco's Bulletin," and the Associated Press to take on this type of work. Later, he became an assistant editor of "Transatlantic Tales, Volta Roman Frederick A' Stokes Co. Adventure Publisher's Syndicate" and an editor of "George H. Doran Co." His first novel was published in 1914, titled "Our Mr. Wrenn." In addition, he also served as a selector for many short story magazines. He wrote a play titled "Hobohemia," which was published in New York in 1919.

Sinclair Lewis's works are most widely circulated among Americans today, and of course, there are also the most people discussing him.

Random Notes on the German Theater Scene 268

Reinhardt Today

Anyone who has studied the art of the stage is probably familiar with the name of this master. In modern drama, Appia and Gordon Craig, along with him, have indeed left great achievements, but what is this master currently engaged in?

Since resigning from the Deutsches Theater in 1922 due to operational difficulties, he has been out of the spotlight for a long time. In his luxurious villa in Charlesbrook, during this period of seeming seclusion, quietly observing the theater scene, he directed Goethe's "Stella" at the Josefstadt Theater in Vienna. This direction achieved a very memorable success in the Vienna theater scene and had a great impact on the Austrian theater scene.

In this "Stella," he had neither "realism in the living dead" nor the "populism" in "Tanton." He left the somber theater scene in Berlin, which represented violence and triviality, and entered Vienna, the capital that tourists still imagine to be from the 18th century. His heart was filled with the beauty of this ancient-style capital. The solidity and elegance of this newly discovered capital really attracted his heart. As a Northerner, he could not forget the beauty of the Italian-style (Carnival). Therefore, he used his Northern classical simplicity to reconcile the innocent tenderness of the Southern country, making the stage of "Stella" like a classical wind stage. The elegant mood of the Italian midsummer night expressed in his direction of "The Merchant of Venice" together made a representative performance of success in this regard. From this, one can see a transformation, which means that the emotions of his genius have been immersed in the world of Mozart's music.

For two years, there have been rumors that he would build a theater to realize his new ambitions. After some twists and turns, he did realize the construction of this theater. On the day of its completion, State Chancellor Marx and Foreign Minister Storerzeman were welcomed in the boxes. The theater opened on this day.

Reinhardt intended for his theater to revive the form of the 18th-century social theater. He wanted to make the theater he presided over a beautiful, ideal, new social theater in Berlin. The special boxes inside the theater had lightning-like rose-colored tubular electric lights embedded in the ceiling, and the corridors were covered in bright red velvet carpets. The theater was very small overall, with a total capacity of only 500 people, 300 in the middle and 200 in the surrounding two-story boxes. The architect who designed it was the famous Oscar Kaufmann, who had built six small theaters in Berlin.

The entire design of this theater followed Reinhardt's ideas. The most distinctive feature was the small boxes that achieved the purpose of a social theater. The velvet curtains, stage curtains, and chair colors inside the theater were all bright red. They were as thin as the color of grass, and when exposed to electric light, they seemed to turn white. The upper and lower parts formed two extremely opposite colors, creating a novel interest. Each box was a small room for only four people, with a small lounge attached outside.

The ceiling was painted with delicate golden patterns, with a glass lamp designed with wisteria flowers hanging in the center. The seats in the middle had only a dozen rows. The orchestra was positioned in the boxes opposite the stage. The audience watched the play from the front but listened to the music from behind or the side. These were all distinctive features that left a deep impression on people in the theater.

The contrasting configuration of bright colors throughout the theater was well received. The boxes, up and down, also had reddish-brown wall paintings on the thin egg-colored walls, tastefully decorated with medieval-style bear decorations and ancient-style stories (sketches) such as moonlight nocturnes and Valkyries with masks. They all carried a Viennese mood and adopted a bit of expressionist style. All of this was full of lightness and smiles, humor and elegance, which was the sentiment held by Reinhardt in his mature artistic realm.

Reinhardt named his theater the "Comedy Theater."

Reinhardt presided over this new and beautiful small theater, creating a new, light-hearted laugh and a bright and elegant atmosphere. Perhaps this is one of the most noteworthy artistic revivals in Germany after the war.

Hurricane Theater 269

The years 1920 and 1921 were the peak of the expressionist movement in German drama. Among them, the most popular play, which was sold out night after night, was the performance of Toller's "Masse Mensch" on the Berlin National Stage. The background and other performances of this play were completely expressionistic. Soon, Hauptmann's "The White Savior" was staged, and the Mexican background above also used expressionist mountains and trees with thorns. This kind of installation continued to be popular in other decorations. For example, in the summer garden "Lurapark" outside Berlin, the mountains installed in the sliding railroad area are exactly this kind of sword-like mountains with painted oil paint. Winding in the vast summer night sky like shadow puppets, they are indeed a novel and magnificent view.

On the streets of Berlin, there were coffee shops and cinemas with expressionist style, as well as several dance halls. Among the bookstores, there were small bookstores labeled "Hurricane." Inside, the permanent exhibition of expressionist or futurist paintings and books was very touching. Needless to say, many expressionist books were displayed in his shop windows.

The "Hurricane Theater" was produced by writers and calligraphers centered on this bookstore. The first performance was "Human" by Lothar Schreyer, an important figure in this school. The entire venue was full on the day of the performance, but most people were only surprised by this extremely cutting-edge expressionist drama and did not necessarily have a complete understanding.

This transformation of "German sorrow" is expressionism, awakening people from the "superhuman world" of individualistic struggle, shouting "Der Mensch" (humanity) to do this art movement with full social consciousness. Achieving all mature effects on the theater, the efforts of the "Hurricane Theater" in extremely cutting-edge expressionist drama should not be considered wasted. (Su) (To be continued)

Art Circle Submission Guidelines 270

(1) The text is limited to news, reviews, and introductions about the latest art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature at home and abroad.

(3) Photos are limited to recent portraits of domestic and foreign writers and their works, as well as various photographs related to the text.

(4) The number of words in each text should not exceed 2,000 at most.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Manuscripts should not be written horizontally, and the characters should not be scribbled. Western writing can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw the illustrations in the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black ink must be used.

(8) Please indicate the "Art Circle Editorial Department" on the manuscript.

(9) Whether the manuscript is published or not, it will generally not be returned. If it needs to be returned, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage stamps should be attached.

Youth Garden

The Bright Society of the College of Law and Politics Strives in Written Work 271

— Written by:

Most people are used to blaming young people, saying they "talk big but do nothing." On the other hand, isn't there a reason for this? Let's see how many academic groups in various schools truly express their strength in practical work. Societies and associations spring up like mushrooms after a rain, but what about the work? Apart from arguing about how to proceed during meetings, once they're over, everyone looks after their own affairs and only cares about their own fun. Some only create wall newspapers with a low-spirited interest as a business for seeking pleasure. This truly shows the lack of discipline among Chinese youth, and it is the greatest shame for us young people.

But now, the students of the Bright Society of the College of Law and Politics are different. They have completely reversed that morbid state, starting with the performance of practical work as a preliminary step. Originally, we had never seen or heard of any Bright Society, nor had we ever seen any of their declarations or announcements. Yet, in the midst of the vigorous formation of small groups at the College of Law and Politics, that "Bright Bi-Monthly" suddenly appeared. How could it not surprise the general student body? Moreover, among the small groups in Shanghai schools, only the "Fa Guang" of the Law Research Society of the Law College can publish such beneficial materials, as far as I know. I think the publication of this "Bright" magazine by the College of Law and Politics may not be without its contribution to the school's reputation.

In terms of thought, this "Bright Bi-Monthly" can still be grasped within a correct scope. In the "Opening Remarks," we know their aim and purpose in publishing this small magazine. First, they feel that the dangerous phenomenon in the current youth community is that countless passionate young people are being sacrificed, and countless passionate young people are dreaming of waking the lion and driving backwards to dig their own graves. In particular, affected by the internal wars, banditry, and the preciousness of gold and cheapness of silver, the general economic situation has shown signs of unrest. The dual panic of youth unemployment and being unable to study is expanding daily. As a result, the entire youth community, due to the instability of thought, is only taking the road of reaction, only seeing hesitation and decadence, and even falling into depravity. Therefore, they believe in this dissatisfaction and want to discuss all the issues concerning the youth themselves. Second, they feel that the current social science movement and literary movement are flowing into abnormal progress, which is extremely dangerous in reality. "We must never advocate class struggle to bring the nation to its death. Therefore, we can only strive for a nationalist literary movement, negatively resisting proletarian literature, and positively awakening national consciousness to promote the realization of nationalism and achieve the goal of national freedom and equality." The third is related to their own problems.

"We feel that in the huge College of Law and Politics, since the autumn semester began two months ago, there have been very few academic or literary groups or publications issued. The atmosphere is really too dull. Students who are naturally quiet have the library and self-study room as their paradise, and perhaps they don't feel the silence. Students who have found their objects of affection have parks and theaters for their wild revelry and sweet words, and perhaps they won't feel the boredom. But besides these, the general students in this not very fluid atmosphere will inevitably feel silent and bored. We want to use the weak power of this magazine to stir up the air in the entire college, hoping that after this magazine, many kinds of valuable publications will appear."

This is their bright attitude. They are moving forward under such bright illumination.

Regarding the content, they all write with a rigorous attitude. Zhu Jianbai's "Questions on the Outline of the Student Union" is based on legal principles, legal precedents, and facts to discuss the sixth provision of the student union outline promulgated by the central government: "The power organ of the student union is the general assembly of members, the representative assembly during the adjournment of the general assembly, and the executive committee during the adjournment of the representative assembly." He believes that it is not very suitable. I think this kind of text discussing regulations is very valuable. Yang Zhigang's "Opinions on Family Law" is a text dedicated to discussing academics. It elaborates on family law in great detail. This is a very long article. Chun Sen's novel "A Letter" only contains some in this issue, but in these few, it seems to be too sentimental. His preface says that this letter belongs to one of his friends. This is perhaps true, because I think Chun Sen will never write such sentimental texts again. This article probably describes the story of a pair of lovers struggling under the old etiquette. I hope that the following can be slightly inclined towards the struggle of will. In addition, there are Zhu Airen's poem "Youth of the Era" and Han Bin's "Rogue and Bookworm," and Wan Bang's "Marriage and Love," etc., are all worth discussing. Gradually improving, it is truly a powerful publication.

After the publication, they immediately distributed it to various faculty members and students, and it was well-received by the general public.

The Guanghua Literary Society 272

— Written by:

The Guanghua Literary Society is a group that studies literature. Membership is not limited to students of any department or major. Anyone who is interested in new literature can join.

The first general meeting of the semester was held shortly after the start of the semester. Although there were only forty or fifty members, the spirit was exceptionally vibrant. They all hoped to do some small work together this semester and no longer be as silent and unknown as the literary society of the past.

The society adopts a committee system, divided into seven departments: chairman, secretary, accounting, library, speech, general affairs, and editing.

The work of the library department is as follows: On the one hand, it collects borrowed books from members, numbers them, and issues a book catalog for members to borrow. On the other hand, it arranges a classroom called the research room for members to read.

The speech department is purely for inviting literary figures to give lectures at the school to enhance the knowledge of members. Initially, it was set at once every two weeks, and Mr. Zhu Yingpeng and Mr. Zhao Jingshen were invited to give lectures. However, members have a particularly high interest in listening to lectures, so it will be changed to once a week in the future, which will be more beneficial for enhancing knowledge.

The work of the editorial department is as follows: It publishes a wall newspaper in the school once a week, publishing some short works and reporting the news of the society's progress. Outside the school, it will publish a monthly magazine and series of books. The supply and arrangement of those manuscripts are probably the responsibility of the members. The monthly magazine is in contact with various bookstores, so it cannot be carried out immediately. As for the series of books, that is not a matter of overnight. As long as members have collections of works, they will be included in the series for publication. According to the latest news, a poetry selection will be published. If members have good works, they can submit them. It is expected to be published during the winter vacation. The deadline for submissions is the end of November.

Shanghai Market

Business News 273

A contribution from the Shanghai office of the Liuhegou Coal Mine Company states that contemporary art giants Sun Changhuang and Gong Youzhen, in view of the needs of the times, have organized a large-scale Shanghai Applied Art Society, setting up three groups: commercial patterns, industrial patterns, and decorative design. For example, trademarks, advertisements and other patterns, storefronts and showcase decorations, dyeing, weaving, ceramics, furniture and printing patterns, residential clothing accessories design, and film, drama, photography and other scene settings, all modern life applied art matters will be complete. As for the industrial and commercial circles, there are even more contributions. The society is located at 66 Sichuan Road, second floor.

The Hanli Company declared that the United States lacked Chinese printing houses, and the printing industry was controlled by foreigners at very high prices. Overseas Chinese documents mostly used Japanese mimeographs, but the printed words were blurry and irreplaceable. At the National Goods Exhibition held by the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in San Francisco, the company sent several Zhongling printing machines for display, and the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, Mr. Deng Zuyin, tested and promoted them. Overseas Chinese in the United States visited the machine with great results. The printed words were simple, clear, and suitable for printing both Chinese and Western characters. At the same time, more than 200 companies placed orders. Now, the Chamber of Commerce has telegraphed to order 300 printing machines. At the same time, the managers of Saigon, Batavia, and the Philippines have also come to purchase machines. The company is in great demand and the inventory is not much. It is working day and night to add to the manufacturing.

Jiufutang, located on Zhejiang Road and Dai Gou Bridge, declares that the company's silk satin, calligraphy screens, and couplets are at great discounts and with great gifts. Silk banners start at two yuan or more, and a pair of real silk stockings is given as a gift for purchasing a festive banner for four yuan or more. Recently, there have been many weddings, and people from all walks of life are enthusiastically placing orders.

The Sino-Western Pharmacy on Fourth Road is holding a grand sale for the second anniversary of the completion of its new building. The discounts on various goods are very low, and the gifts are very common. It is said that the first and second prize winners are heard of every day, and it is difficult to count the winners of other prizes. As a result, customers are like clouds, and the business is booming.

Guanshengyuan Food Company, located on South Sixth Road, declares that the restaurant department on the upper floor of the company's main store has recently agreed with Xiaoguanyuan in Jiangwan to sell various famous chrysanthemums, with no fewer than five or six hundred varieties. The department has specially used wooden frames to pile up chrysanthemums into mountains, with colorful and fragrant aromas filling the seat. Being in it is like being in a sea of fragrances. In order to meet the occasion, the department has specially sent a commissioner to search for a large number of authentic hairy crabs in the Yangcheng Lake area for all walks of life to come and hold crabs and admire chrysanthemums. In the past two days, the sales of both crabs and chrysanthemums have been very prosperous.

Theater News 274

The Xifan Film Company declares that the second collection of the company's great production, Golden Rooster Ridge, is Blood Splattered on Golden Rooster Ridge, which is the proud work of the famous director Hu Zongli, starring the martial arts female star Wang Feijuan. This film was previewed last night and the results were better than the first collection. Ms. Wang also has amazing performances in the film. The drama was adapted by Ren Jinpin from Qing Dynasty sword fairy martial arts stories, and the plot is tortuous and interesting. The photography also has the latest contributions, which can fully exhaust the magic of illusion.

The Paris Grand Theater declares that the latest production of the Niaofa Company, Hell on Earth, will be screened at the theater today. The film stars the female lead of Floating Earth, Camiran; the male lead of Lustful Sea and Passionate Sky, Flori Hsu; and the male lead of Prodigal Son's History, Warwick Huai. Not only is the plot tortuous and the performance profound, but the meaning is also alarming and thought-provoking. It is truly a masterpiece that contributes to the world. The interpolations, such as the grasshopper dancing and the ants working, are especially novel spectacles on the screen.

The Audian Company declares that since the appearance of The Love Parade, there is no one who does not know the peerless beauty McDonald. McDonald was a stage actress who was famous for her singing, and her beauty was especially loved by the world. Therefore, she had already become famous in stage plays and was called a peerless talent. Only the film audience did not know her, so they were indifferent and did not pay attention. After the advent of sound films, the great director Lubitsch used his intelligence and directed The Love Parade with all his heart, using McDonald as the female lead of the film. Thus, this unparalleled beauty jumped to become a film star. The film was completed with the beautiful singing voice, the brilliant appearance, the supple body, the elegant demeanor, the profound performance, and the alluring beauty. It was admired by audiences all over the world, and almost everyone wanted to worship her. She became the great screen lover in the dreams of men. Now, her starring role in "Let's Go Native" has come to Shanghai and has been purchased by the company at a high price. It is scheduled to be screened at the company's newly established Xinguang Grand Theater. The film's vivid depictions and wonderful plots tell a tortuous story and showcase beautiful scenes. Everything is unusual, and the deep meaning and taste are especially unique. The comedy performances, the wonderful dances, and the clear and beautiful songs are not comparable to other sound films. It is expected that when this film is screened at the Xinguang Grand Theater, McDonald's name will become even more prominent.

The Zhabei Qingyun Road Corner World Grand Theater declares that the theater will change to the Shangwu fighting machine film Black Knight starting today. The film is the latest production of the Jinan Film Company, starring Ye Juanjuan, Huang Yunzhen, and others. It takes chivalry as the warp and love as the weft, and the performances of the actors all match the plot. It is the most valuable masterpiece produced by the company.

Home
